The additional four garments of the High Priest were multi-colored: the breastplate was white, blue, red, and gold; the coat was blue wool. One who tore them was liable to punishment. The garments themselves provided atonement for the mistakes of the Jews. One can learn moral lessons from them and from the other vessels in the Temple. For example, the Ark was gold on the inside and outside to tell us that any Torah scholar whose outside is not the same as his inside - that is, who is insincere - is not a true Torah scholar.<br />
<br />
In general, the Torah itself can be a cure for some but poison for others. This is the meaning of the phrase, “And this is the Torah that Moses put (‘sam’) in front of the Jews.” The word “sam” means a drug of any kind and can cure or kill. Some say that one should learn it for the right reasons, and others - that he should understand it deeply enough. 


<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;Portrait of a Man in Oriental Garment &nbsp;By Rembrandt Van Rijn

---

### content/yoma/73.txt
<a id="src-00286"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/73.txt`

Yoma 73 - Urim VeTumim
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggIVu6k6XQm3_SufN_BmyTyAxZTMJ9cMIznozfzmwFRuPAAG1gHV639q4QJWKVwEGtLTUkQ21cjKsvHNBuGR0ZNCbUaW18WvgawLRZm72zWwGWVvnmwIBsHBmDjKYWuOf5v08oYSRDFePC/s1600/To+Decide+the+Question+By+John+George+Brown.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="238" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggIVu6k6XQm3_SufN_BmyTyAxZTMJ9cMIznozfzmwFRuPAAG1gHV639q4QJWKVwEGtLTUkQ21cjKsvHNBuGR0ZNCbUaW18WvgawLRZm72zWwGWVvnmwIBsHBmDjKYWuOf5v08oYSRDFePC/s1600/To+Decide+the+Question+By+John+George+Brown.jpg" width="320" /></a>The same eight garments of the High Priest discussed so far were also needed when consulting Urim VeTumim. Incidentally, the Kohen appointed for battle would go with the Jews to war and wear the same eight garments. After the war, he continued to serve in the Temple in the same outfit. Others say that he does not serve in the Temple at all. We cannot permit him to be like the High Priest because the real High Priest will feel bad about it. Neither can he wear the garments of a regular Kohen because they only raise in the level of holiness but never bring down.
<br />
<br />
Back to Urim VeTumim, what was it? Some say that inside the High Priest's breastplate, they put a piece of parchment with the name of God written on it, others - that it refers to the precious stones on the breastplate. The High Priest would be wearing it, the king would ask a question, and the answer would be formed by the letters protruding forward. Some say that only a worthy High Priest could see them protrude and then interpreted the answer. 
<br />
<br />
Art: To Decide the Question By John George Brown

---

### content/yoma/74.txt
<a id="src-00287"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/74.txt`

Yoma 74 - How to properly afflict oneself
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgrcIUmx1fCjg-BmP-Qthvh2Nikv15pp921xX7BjTvJd5tt3m0TrQjI5OLjk2MvuZwYeOhLGmop95AdIwLs6wM8wPX8Q-IeFQx7Ffc2I2iJshyyRQyeWlSAUg1wz5xqcSrwiovh_vR3MjIn/s1600/Thirst+By+William-Adolphe+Bouguereau.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgrcIUmx1fCjg-BmP-Qthvh2Nikv15pp921xX7BjTvJd5tt3m0TrQjI5OLjk2MvuZwYeOhLGmop95AdIwLs6wM8wPX8Q-IeFQx7Ffc2I2iJshyyRQyeWlSAUg1wz5xqcSrwiovh_vR3MjIn/s1600/Thirst+By+William-Adolphe+Bouguereau.jpg" width="239" /></a>On Yom Kippur, one is forbidden to eat and drink, wash oneself, anoint his body with oil, wear leather shoes, and have marital relations. Just forbidden, you say? But it is more than this; one is liable to be cut off from the Jewish people and from his spiritual source! - The rule above is talking about a small amount, which is still forbidden. OK, this answer is good, according to those who say that a small amount of forbidden food is actually prohibited by the Torah. However, if the Torah does not mind a small amount, what is this rule talking about? It is still prohibited by the Sages.
<br />
<br />
What is the basis for this disagreement? Rabbi Yochanan says that since small amounts do add to the amount which is prohibited by the Torah, it must be that these small amounts are themselves prohibited, for otherwise, where does the prohibition come from? However, Resh Lakish says that eating a small amount is not called “eating,” Thus, it is simply not included in the prohibition. 
<br />
<br />
So how is one supposed to “afflict his soul?” Perhaps it means sitting in the sun on a hot day or in the shade on a cold one? - No, the nature of the required suffering is such that one refrain from such activities as eating, drinking, etc., but not that one actively seeks out to increase his suffering. 
<br />
<br />
Art: Thirst By William-Adolphe Bouguereau

---

### content/yoma/75.txt
<a id="src-00288"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/75.txt`

Yoma 75 - The affliction of manna
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEir5jp6QHuUL-Ftfz63q-4gqrzTq6rXzI5HXS-WK-3W6GhmBXnmvVRj2MtyZdJtKilZI4cpmAHejT1ypSghw0LFeDWv3dM10thUJ_7TK7NvWREsd3z1jifuU_eqA2uGpT083rXruE6Th41-/s1600/The+Gathering+of+the+Manna+By+Bernardino+Luini.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEir5jp6QHuUL-Ftfz63q-4gqrzTq6rXzI5HXS-WK-3W6GhmBXnmvVRj2MtyZdJtKilZI4cpmAHejT1ypSghw0LFeDWv3dM10thUJ_7TK7NvWREsd3z1jifuU_eqA2uGpT083rXruE6Th41-/s1600/The+Gathering+of+the+Manna+By+Bernardino+Luini.jpg" width="249" /></a>In discussing food afflictions of Yom Kippur, the Talmud turns to manna, since it, too, is called an affliction: “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=8#P5148">Who feeds you manna in the Wilderness… to afflict you</a>.” - Some say it is because they never knew what they will eat tomorrow, should manna not fall the next day. Others - that since manna could take on any taste but always looked the same, they were never satisfied with it. Rav Yosef (who was blind) demonstrates that a blind person eats but is never fully satisfied.
<br />
<br />
More parallel disagreements: what does this phrase mean, “Worry in one’s heart? - Quash it!” Some say that it sounds like “remove from your mind” - by studying the Torah. Others - to tell it to others. But how does this help? - Since others will suffer from hearing about your troubles, and they don’t deserve it, God will remove it from you to spare them this unwarranted suffering.
<br />
<br />
More facts about manna are drawn from the words describing it. For example, it was “like bread, oil, and honey.” How can it be? For young people, it felt like bread, for old - like oil, and for children - like honey, each according to the age preference.
<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;The Gathering of the Manna By Bernardino Luini

---

### content/yoma/76.txt
<a id="src-00289"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/76.txt`

Yoma 76 - Why was manna given daily
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2eSRF_myCXqCYRBefRaMrp_pGLqllHRSNBUp8T9khcT_q8w3DS9M90ZqZMAa66peb1nV6sQeJ-z55Q1QK8sam-CBkmFSgX7PDH5lHrqxYJtU6_KA_03Mr7ujEqnp1Xvcp6l2LzNGjh4JC/s1600/A+bottle+of+wine+By+French+School.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="258" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2eSRF_myCXqCYRBefRaMrp_pGLqllHRSNBUp8T9khcT_q8w3DS9M90ZqZMAa66peb1nV6sQeJ-z55Q1QK8sam-CBkmFSgX7PDH5lHrqxYJtU6_KA_03Mr7ujEqnp1Xvcp6l2LzNGjh4JC/s1600/A+bottle+of+wine+By+French+School.jpg" width="320" /></a>The students of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai asked him a question, “Why did the manna have to be given every day?” He told them, “I will give you a parable. A king had a son, and he gave him his allowance once for the whole year. Consequently, his son visited him only once a year. The king then changed to giving him money daily, and now the son visited him every day. So too the Jews: one who had four or five children would worry, thinking, perhaps the manna will not fall tomorrow, and they will die of starvation. Thus, the Israelites now directed their hearts to God at all times.” Others say so that it would be warm and fresh. Yet others - so that they did not have to carry it.
<br />
<br />
Earlier, we mentioned the five things that one is should abstain from on Yom Kippur: <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2014/01/yoma-74-how-to-properly-afflict-oneself.html">food, drink, washing</a>, etc. Where does it say so in the Torah? - It could be that it is not explicitly mentioned in the Torah, but because the term “deprivation” is mentioned five times, the Sages decreed five deprivations that one should sustain. Food, however, is named explicitly, and drinking is included together with eating. How do we know this last fact? - Because Torah mentioned drinking wine and put it in the list of food items.
<br />
<br />
Incidentally, wine makes one wise, and excessive drinking leads to poverty. This is reflected in the word “tirosh” used for wine. If one deserves, it makes him “rosh” - head; if not - it makes him “rash” - poor.
<br />
<br />
Art: A bottle of wine By French School

---

### content/yoma/77.txt
<a id="src-00290"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/77.txt`

Yoma 77 - Crossing the river to see one’s teacher
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgR7hN1RoECz-UkWC0XKdv88tH02HTQjG3C_69NKwU6zhtx1XEVkKyeE6QKYCwA2NIvgKiKAJHPvYUvCiWDyCNvyyWDk_EW27VmvgD9JkRfh9Dn_DGmid70NMMeUKUwwN8fwxjChidBoq3H/s1600/Figures+crossing+a+frozen+river+By+Louis+Pierre+Verwee.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="244" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgR7hN1RoECz-UkWC0XKdv88tH02HTQjG3C_69NKwU6zhtx1XEVkKyeE6QKYCwA2NIvgKiKAJHPvYUvCiWDyCNvyyWDk_EW27VmvgD9JkRfh9Dn_DGmid70NMMeUKUwwN8fwxjChidBoq3H/s1600/Figures+crossing+a+frozen+river+By+Louis+Pierre+Verwee.jpg" width="320" /></a>To prove that abstaining from washing and anointing oneself is called an affliction, the Talmud quotes&nbsp;<a href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt3410.htm">Daniel</a>, who afflicted himself in this way. It then continues with these verses, which tell the story of the angel Gabriel being expelled from the Heavenly court but brought back “because of the words of Daniel.”
<br />
<br />
Daniel was shown in a vision that twenty-five people were standing in the Temple, bowing to the sun in the east, with their backs toward the Temple on the west. Since their faces were to the east, we already know that their backs were to the west; why is this mentioned? The real story was that they bared themselves and defecated toward the Temple as an additional sign of contempt. The Holy One Blessed be He said to the angel Michael, “Your nation has sinned!” Michael suggested to spare the nation because of the good ones among them, but the answer was, “I will burn them together with the good ones who did not protest.” At this time, Gabriel asked another angel, a Cherub, to bring the coals, took those coals, and threw them on Jerusalem. However, since the coals cooled somewhat, the nation survived. They gave Gabriel sixty fiery lashes (pulsa d’nura) and expelled him. Gabriel continued arguing on behalf of the Jewish people, and when he mentioned Daniel, the Holy One Blessed be He asked, “Who is he that is advocating on behalf of my children?” - and Gabriel was brought back. As a result, however, Persians, and especially later Greeks, were given dominion. 
<br />
<br />
Even though washing is forbidden, if one wants to visit his father or his teacher on Yom Kippur, and a river separates them, he can cross even if the water reaches his neck. He is even allowed to go back since otherwise, he will refrain from going in the future. Only washing for pleasure is actually forbidden.
<br />
<br />
Art: Figures crossing a frozen river By Louis Pierre Verwee

---

### content/yoma/78.txt
<a id="src-00291"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/78.txt`

Yoma 78 - Shoes
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj2Ljoz2nmGnzisG3BmZ-1_Z1g5U_6U7jned9kXLKxshwU2Z9U5YP_hVDRn3j2EhROwT2rsCKF37CaJCImSgQVD8O53sVBP1AUjsQYhd1bZjBlah11LuHGqIAs1cMkIWYki9MJV_MkQ6Bmg/s1600/Still+life,+a+pair+of+shoes+by+Vincent+Van+Gogh.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="249" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj2Ljoz2nmGnzisG3BmZ-1_Z1g5U_6U7jned9kXLKxshwU2Z9U5YP_hVDRn3j2EhROwT2rsCKF37CaJCImSgQVD8O53sVBP1AUjsQYhd1bZjBlah11LuHGqIAs1cMkIWYki9MJV_MkQ6Bmg/s1600/Still+life,+a+pair+of+shoes+by+Vincent+Van+Gogh.jpg" width="320" /></a>One is not supposed to wear shoes on Yom Kippur. Perhaps this is one of the reasons why wading through a river is allowed - because one won’t come to carry his shoes, should they fall off? What about Shabbat - can one cross the river, given that now he has shoes and might potentially carry them? Nehemiah saw Rav Ami and Rav Asi cross a pool of water on Shabbat. The actual incident with someone trustworthy is the best proof, and so this is accepted. What about sandals that slip off easier? - there, it is preferable not to cross the river in them. Here is an actual story about it.
<br />
<br />
A Jewish ruler (Exilarch) n Babylonia came to the city of Hagronia and lectured there. All the Sages came to his lecture, except Ravina. Since Ravina may have offended the Exilarch, Rafram came to exonerate him and asked him why he missed the lecture. Ravina answered that his foot was hurting. “Then you should have put on a shoe!” - “It was the top of the foot.” “Then you should use a (loose) sandal!” - To this Ravina answered, “There was a pool there, and it is preferable not to cross a pool in a sandal on Shabbat.” 
<br />
<br />
The standard material used for making shoes is leather. When talking about not wearing shoes on Yom Kippur, do we mean only leather shoes or perhaps any kind of shoes? Again, an actual story helps: Rav Yitzchak saw Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi wearing shoes made out of rush (reed) on Yom Kippur. And yet, some say that all kinds of shoes were meant.
<br />
<br />
Art: Still life, a pair of shoes by Vincent Van Gogh

---

### content/yoma/79.txt
<a id="src-00292"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/79.txt`

Yoma 79 - How much to eat on Yom Kippur?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj7DYyrenECw_VBiShyphenhyphenHk7WxxLCjXmZv82SVykSzc2heSgWqIR7SDlZ7YB3EoMYe4oFVQXwAx51_Weo7-JJePH1SLcqanYUpGPDwgJjhl3XOfcMecTN7P-N8Y6kXkvaojXcMwIeeSgut4rD/s1600/Still+Life+Of+Porcelain+Bowls+Containing+Sugared+Dates,+Grapes,+And+Oranges+By+French+School.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="238" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj7DYyrenECw_VBiShyphenhyphenHk7WxxLCjXmZv82SVykSzc2heSgWqIR7SDlZ7YB3EoMYe4oFVQXwAx51_Weo7-JJePH1SLcqanYUpGPDwgJjhl3XOfcMecTN7P-N8Y6kXkvaojXcMwIeeSgut4rD/s1600/Still+Life+Of+Porcelain+Bowls+Containing+Sugared+Dates,+Grapes,+And+Oranges+By+French+School.jpg" width="320" /></a>How much does one have to eat on Yom Kippur to be liable? - The volume of food equal to a large date.
<br />
<br />
Rav Pappa wondered, “Date with the pit or without?” A similar question was asked by Rav Ashi about a human bone the size of a barley seed, which makes one ritually impure. Rav Ashi asked, “Dry seed or moist? With the shell or without?”
<br />
<br />
Note that each of the Sages did not have any problem with the other one’s question. Rav Ashi would tell you that “large date” implies as large as it can be, that is, with the seed. In turn, Rav Pappa would retort that a fresh barley seed has a different name, “shibboleth,” and one with the shell is called “ushla.” So the choice of the words itself in the rule already gives them the answer.
<br />
<br />
And why specifically, a large date is used as a measure of prohibition for Yom Kippur? After all, it is less than an egg and is thus not considered a meal!? - The Sages estimated that this volume cools off the hungry person's&nbsp;mind, although it does not satisfy him completely.<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;Still Life Of Porcelain Bowls Containing Sugared Dates, Grapes, And Oranges By French School

---

### content/yoma/8.txt
<a id="src-00293"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/8.txt`

Yoma 8 - Tzitz
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgxnRzJ1lMSvqt8eDToIUc2C47Pq8N32ygH6PQYQz-kog0Z_0MH-x134e-qYtAW9QBfo3A3AvU6KFRuMAojt_8-yEY9d7IbGb8vfvewvt84i-9_kMbZfAKkxSo9epYj3YcrITV_GMLGyXxm/s1600/Yemeni+Jew,++1914+National+Geographic+Magazine.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgxnRzJ1lMSvqt8eDToIUc2C47Pq8N32ygH6PQYQz-kog0Z_0MH-x134e-qYtAW9QBfo3A3AvU6KFRuMAojt_8-yEY9d7IbGb8vfvewvt84i-9_kMbZfAKkxSo9epYj3YcrITV_GMLGyXxm/s320/Yemeni+Jew,++1914+National+Geographic+Magazine.jpg" width="221" /></a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Priestly_golden_head_plate">Tzitz</a> is the golden head plate worn by the High Priest. It fixes the defects of the sacrifices so that even those sacrifices that were not normally acceptable become so with the help of the Tzitz. This is expressed by the Torah as follows, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=28#P2329">So that Aaron will bear the sin of the sacred offerings</a>.”
<br />
<br />
However, which offerings could the Tzitz make kosher? If the priest bringing it wanted to eat it in the wrong place, it “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=19#P3286">would not be acceptable</a>,” and if he even wanted to eat it at the wrong time, it “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=7#P2895">would not be considered</a>.” Thus, the only problem that the Tzitz could fix was the offering that became ritually impure.
<br />
<br />
Did the Tzitz have to be on the forehead of the High Priest to be effective? That depends on the understanding of the word “always (Aaron will wear it).” You can understand that whenever Aaron wears it, it is effective, but not otherwise. Or, you can say that “always” means “constantly when possible,” but even when it is not possible to wear it (such as during sleep), it still works. The Talmud tries to resolve its earlier question,&nbsp;<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/11/yoma-7-is-everything-permitted.html">whether the laws of purity are completely abrogated or if they only allow a few exceptions</a>, using the laws of Tzitz, but alas, Tzitz allows both interpretations. Incidentally, from Tzitz, we derive that one who wears <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tefillin">tefillin</a> must be constantly mindful of them.
<br />
<br />
Art: Yemeni Jew,  1914 National Geographic Magazine.

---

### content/yoma/80.txt
<a id="src-00294"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/80.txt`

Yoma 80 - One, who tries to get a little, will succeed
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgmNXVHTPRxbBHq9LXbt7apC8SgjY9xEtSrjls_FSOyRae8_VxHHGWVEHj5DMYBlLRDRhPELHjYZ5h8Ev-lswvKSEvL3Bs2LslaPtR3B6Y5WP5JwHKRxWPDm9rhTPqbu0GP9FgFSt-_Ae7C/s1600/A+lady+seated+in+an+interior,+with+a+maidservant+and+a+girl+holding+a+chicken+and+basket+of+eggs+By+(after)+Tibout+Regters.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgmNXVHTPRxbBHq9LXbt7apC8SgjY9xEtSrjls_FSOyRae8_VxHHGWVEHj5DMYBlLRDRhPELHjYZ5h8Ev-lswvKSEvL3Bs2LslaPtR3B6Y5WP5JwHKRxWPDm9rhTPqbu0GP9FgFSt-_Ae7C/s1600/A+lady+seated+in+an+interior,+with+a+maidservant+and+a+girl+holding+a+chicken+and+basket+of+eggs+By+(after)+Tibout+Regters.jpg" width="247" /></a><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/10/chullin-118-hide-and-gravy.html">We have seen</a> that to transmit ritual impurity, the food must have at least the volume of an egg. But, how do we know this?
<br />
<br />
Since the Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=11#P3029">Any food that is eaten</a>,” we understand that we are talking about food coming from another food. And what is it? - Chicken egg: it is food, and it comes from another food, a chicken. But maybe it is a young goat, which comes from its mother, who is also food? - No, it does not just "come," but it requires slaughter. But perhaps it is an egg of a bar-yuchani bird, which is as big as sixty cities? - No, because we have a rule: one, who tries to grab a little, succeeds in that, and may even be added more, but one who tries to grab a lot - he may not be given anything at all, and so we have to limit ourselves to a chicken egg. But perhaps the Torah meant an egg of a tiny bird?
<br />
<br />
The last question is indeed irrefutable, and we abandon this complete chain of questions and answers. Rather, “Any food that is eaten” implies that it is eaten in one gulp, and the Sages estimated that the throat cannot hold more than a hen’s egg.
<br />
<br />
Back to measures of food for which one bears responsibility if he eats it on Yom Kippur: solids in the amount of a large date, and liquid - a full cheek. How can we have one measure that depends on an objective average large date and another - on his personal cheek capacity? - The Sages estimated that this much would assuage the suffering of the fast, and less than that would not. This is even true for a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Og">giant called Og</a>, whose full cheek was huge but whose limit of solid on Yom Kippur would also be a large date.<br />
<br />
Art: A lady seated in an interior, with a maidservant and a girl holding a chicken and basket of eggs By (after) Tibout Regters

---

### content/yoma/81.txt
<a id="src-00295"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/81.txt`

Yoma 81 - How to eat on Yom Kippur and not bear responsibility
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjYGUPrsI4BJY3Thp49IC36xqE2Vl35iij_3wftJ70zeRmTLNXo1MV0VBP3OWOw6wqvbvhlO6fA54-ZdRQfxawqp2JCC5jdve8CN_KzjstLTM2pYUQLYm5LUYb3JDSfMn9PC0BO7dDsq6U3/s800/Annibale+Carracci%2527s+-++Il+Mangiafagioli.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="654" data-original-width="800" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjYGUPrsI4BJY3Thp49IC36xqE2Vl35iij_3wftJ70zeRmTLNXo1MV0VBP3OWOw6wqvbvhlO6fA54-ZdRQfxawqp2JCC5jdve8CN_KzjstLTM2pYUQLYm5LUYb3JDSfMn9PC0BO7dDsq6U3/s320/Annibale+Carracci%2527s+-++Il+Mangiafagioli.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>If one eats excessively on Yom Kippur, stuffing himself with food, he is not liable. The Torah prohibited eating to alleviate hunger, but what he is doing cannot be properly called eating, but rather damaging, both his body and food.<p></p><p>If one both ate and drank, in the same period of forgetfulness - either he forgot it was Yom Kippur or forgot that it is not allowed to eat or drink - it counts as only one transgression. That is because both eating and drinking are covered by the same prohibition of "afflicting oneself by hunger." When he realizes what he has done, he would have to bring one sin-offering.</p><p>However, if he ate and worked, these are two separate prohibitions, and for this, he will have to bring two sin-offerings. If he ate something that people normally don't eat (like spoiled meat) or drank something that people normally don't drink (like fish brine), he is not liable to any sacrifice.</p><p>When one prepares for Yom Kippur on the day before, he gets a double reward. The Torah said, "You will fast on the ninth of the month." But the fast is on the tenth! This shows you that the one who eats and drinks on the ninth gets a reward as if he fasted for two days in a row.</p><p>Art: Il Mangiafagioli by Annibale Carracci's</p>

---

### content/yoma/82.txt
<a id="src-00296"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/82.txt`

Yoma 82 - Children do not fast on Yom Kippur
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><br /></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivyXLa1jpqx9DAyvjO1ZUZFYP6gND_GwdwhRKicEQ0AFL06B5etJacoVqILncUhAvVoN1PHefybr2kt069txy9yyNT-iTmMVVMd9460-7UN-SNRxoRuRIh1MFveJEpD4GJbsCO8T1u91m-/s1243/Children+eating+a+pie+by.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="1243" data-original-width="1000" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivyXLa1jpqx9DAyvjO1ZUZFYP6gND_GwdwhRKicEQ0AFL06B5etJacoVqILncUhAvVoN1PHefybr2kt069txy9yyNT-iTmMVVMd9460-7UN-SNRxoRuRIh1MFveJEpD4GJbsCO8T1u91m-/s320/Children+eating+a+pie+by.jpg" /></a></div>Children are not required to fast on Yom Kippur; in fact, the adults do not allow them to fast. However, they are trained one or two years before their Bar or Bat mitzvah by delaying the day's first meal.<p></p><p>If a pregnant woman craves a certain food on Yom Kippur, we assume that the baby wants it and that withholding it puts her and the fetus in danger. Therefore, they feed her that food until she feels better.&nbsp;</p><p>A sick person on Yom Kippur - if the experts say that he would be in danger if he does not eat, they give him food. If there are no experts there - they ask him. If there is a disagreement between him and the experts, his opinion wins.</p><p>In general, one can violate any Torah's prohibition to save a life - with three exceptions: idol worship,&nbsp; illicit relations, and murder. Where do we learn this from?</p><p>Idol worship. The words of the "Shema" - "You shall love God your Lord with all your heart, all your soul, and all your possessions" mean that one should give up his soul or possessions but not worship idols.</p><p>Murder prohibition is derived from logic. If a governor tells one to kill a person or be killed himself, one should allow himself to be killed but not become a murderer. How does one know that his blood is redder than that of the other person?</p><p>Connected to murder is the law of prohibited relations: a betrothed maiden can be saved from rape at the cost of her pursuer's life. "<a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=22#P5492" target="_blank">The betrothed maiden cried out, but there was no rescuer</a>" - had there been a rescuer, he would be allowed to save her even by killing the assailant. However, if he can stave the attacker without killing him, he would be obligated to do so.</p><p>Art: Children eating a pie by Bartolomé Esteban Murillo</p>

---

### content/yoma/83.txt
<a id="src-00297"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/83.txt`

Yoma 83 - Hand washing after the meal (maim acharonim)
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi6Knlk5CpcmptJQv7nO52hUJrjlryw74aRc8IYzUI7bMMlsHmmMYu15frOPYeJw91_x4b0eDmNLPPxmMvN2TCezZTTmLxZAa6C-UMnZIBvW7QrZhnf6Bc_5u-f-wPOVGB3RHzbIhMjwXfp/s840/The+Shepherd+Meal.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="840" data-original-width="698" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi6Knlk5CpcmptJQv7nO52hUJrjlryw74aRc8IYzUI7bMMlsHmmMYu15frOPYeJw91_x4b0eDmNLPPxmMvN2TCezZTTmLxZAa6C-UMnZIBvW7QrZhnf6Bc_5u-f-wPOVGB3RHzbIhMjwXfp/s320/The+Shepherd+Meal.jpg" /></a></div>Any possible danger to life supersedes the laws of Shabbat and the laws of Kashrut. For example, if one was seized by a fit called "bulmos," which reduces one's eyesight, he must be fed any food, non-kosher if it is closer. However, on Yom Kippur, they give it in small amounts.<p></p><p>Rabbi Yehudah and Rabbi Yose were once on the road. Bulmos seized Rabbi Yehudah, and he ate all the food of a nearby shepherd. Rabbi Yose remarked, "You cleaned up this shepherd!' When they arrived at a city, bulmos seized Rabbi Yose. The city residents surrounded him with all kinds of dishes. Now Rabbi Yehudah said, "I cleaned up a shepherd, but you clean up the city."</p><p>The same Rabbis were once traveling with Rabbi Meir. They arrived at an inn whose owner's name was Kidor. Rabbi Meir considered this a bad name because of the phrase "Kidor" - <a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=32#P5773" target="_blank">because they are a generation that cannot be trusted</a>&nbsp;and did not trust Kidor with his purse. Instead, Rabbi Meir hid the purse at the Kidor father's grave. Kidor's father appeared to his son in a dream and told him to go appropriate the purse. Kidor asked the Rabbis about the dream's meaning, and they told him that Friday night dreams mean nothing. Instead, Rabbi Meir guarded his purse all of Shabbat.</p><p>The other two Rabbis did trust Kidor with their purses, and the next day he denied getting them. They saw some lentils on his beard (because he did not do washing hands after the meal.) They went to Kidor's wife and told her that Kidor instructed to give them their purses, and as proof, they said that she fed him lentils. She gave them the purses, and Kidor killed his wife.&nbsp;</p><p>Rabbi Yose and Rabbi Yehudah then asked Rabbi Meir why he did not warn them. He said that the name is enough for one to be suspicious but not to tell bad things to others.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;The Shepherd’s Meal by George Morland</p>

---

### content/yoma/84.txt
<a id="src-00298"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/84.txt`

Yoma 84 - How Rabbi Yochanan fooled a sorceress
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgu3QKdnK5jzcPMfz9C-b62fFhDMlJEDPB9etL28rlUW4F65dztCQcrtz8GDjyEJLK3yKEJHII0w2emXACF1LOVn-g-tOHMmo9KCkVmfvfaHuFZMPQc2rRn4PbHY_M_CTBePOZLQQde1hbe/s900/the-remedy-benjamin-west-clinedinst.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="900" data-original-width="882" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgu3QKdnK5jzcPMfz9C-b62fFhDMlJEDPB9etL28rlUW4F65dztCQcrtz8GDjyEJLK3yKEJHII0w2emXACF1LOVn-g-tOHMmo9KCkVmfvfaHuFZMPQc2rRn4PbHY_M_CTBePOZLQQde1hbe/s320/the-remedy-benjamin-west-clinedinst.jpg" /></a></div>Rabbi Yochanan contracted an illness that results in throat pain. He went to a noblewoman who gave him the remedy on Thursday and on Friday. He asked about the Shabbat (when he was busy with the students and could not visit her), but she said he would not need it on Shabbat. He pressed her to tell him the medicine, and she said, "Swear that you will not reveal it." He said, "To the God of Israel, I will not reveal it." Then he went ahead and taught it publicly. How could he do it? - He meant, "To the God of Israel I will not reveal it, but to His people, I will." But she would still accuse him, and it would be bad publicity that a Rabbi did it!? - He told her immediately that his oath was not valid.<p></p><p>If a building collapsed on Shabbat and they don't know if somebody was trapped there, and furthermore if he was dead or alive - they violate Shabbat for any doubt about the life-threatening condition. If they find him alive, they keep clearing away the rubble even if it extends his life just a little, but if he is dead, they leave him there.</p><p>Art: The remedy by Benjamin West Clinedinst</p><div><br /></div>

---

### content/yoma/85.txt
<a id="src-00299"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/85.txt`

Yoma 85 - For what does Yom Kippur forgive?
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg9aS1b1dzd3KnwBrFqo-UBFHVI-pFIKmE_eiVlpynlpS2dZkUxdEtVM1HaJoMp1Qe2g41nnmtSgGa3NUdncjgPrHSiuC4lJC5t0sJQvC4XK9275drcxT15KdNFBrC0NLoeZT2L65SxCdSx/s1316/After+the+Misdeed+by+Jean+Beraud.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="1080" data-original-width="1316" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg9aS1b1dzd3KnwBrFqo-UBFHVI-pFIKmE_eiVlpynlpS2dZkUxdEtVM1HaJoMp1Qe2g41nnmtSgGa3NUdncjgPrHSiuC4lJC5t0sJQvC4XK9275drcxT15KdNFBrC0NLoeZT2L65SxCdSx/s320/After+the+Misdeed+by+Jean+Beraud.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>Yom Kippur is the Day of Atonement. It is a means to achieve a clean slate. Other means for it are listed below.<p></p><p>If one does something listed as "Don't do it" in the Torah, and that is also qualified as "his soul will be cut off from the people" - then, if he did it inadvertently, he brings an offering in the Temple and is forgiven. When there is no Temple, his repentance is enough, and he is completely forgiven on Yom Kippur.</p><p>If it is a regular "Do it" or "Don't do it," and he violates it, then his repentance is effective right away, even before Yom Kippur.</p><p>If he tries to use this rule to his advantage and says, "I will do the wrong thing, but I will then repent," - a chance to repent may not happen.&nbsp;</p><p>The above is true only in regards to himself. However, if he wrongs his fellow man, Yom Kippur does not atone until he pacifies his fellow.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;After the Misdeed by Jean Beraud</p>

---

### content/yoma/86.txt

Yoma 86 - Desecration of God's name
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_omgLB8sZ_naFKPUpJEGo4CyE2RF-Wgzj-P3KlzRCLiGXfifnug6qdLTE6NHuSY-4DUteDQc_No9jVwjZpmvpCd0F2FPP-ru6MwamnJu58MyzVLyD8tFy_C_XPCt77gMNrWk0Sa9JKf24/s900/a-scholar-in-his-study-thomas-wyck.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="900" data-original-width="814" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_omgLB8sZ_naFKPUpJEGo4CyE2RF-Wgzj-P3KlzRCLiGXfifnug6qdLTE6NHuSY-4DUteDQc_No9jVwjZpmvpCd0F2FPP-ru6MwamnJu58MyzVLyD8tFy_C_XPCt77gMNrWk0Sa9JKf24/s320/a-scholar-in-his-study-thomas-wyck.jpg" /></a></div>Desecration of God's name, or "<i>Chillul Hashem,</i>" occurs when people say, "Look at what so-and-so did," and it reflects badly on God. For example, this is common when an observant Jew does something wrong. There are various means of atonement for it, such as Yom Kippur, suffering, death, or better, the study of the Torah and teaching it to others.<div><br /></div><div>It also depends on the person. For example, Rav, a prominent Torah scholar in Babilonia, said that <i>Hillul Hashem</i> occurs when a scholar like him does not pay the butcher's bill on time. The reason is, such behavior will lead the butcher to suspect stealing. Abbaye said, "This applies only in the city where the customers bring money to the butcher. But if the custom is for the butcher to go and collect money owed, this is not a problem."</div><div><br /></div><div>On the positive side, one should accumulate wisdom and deal with people pleasantly. What do the people then say? - Happy is the father who taught him Torah; happy is the teacher who taught him Torah. To him applies the phrase, "<a href="https://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt1049.htm" target="_blank">You are my servant, Israel, through whom I am glorified</a>."</div><div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;A scholar in his Study by Thomas Wyck</div>

---

### content/yoma/87.txt
<a id="src-00301"></a>

**Source file:** `content/yoma/87.txt`

Yoma 87 - Saying “excuse me”
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj0KqG4lDazRgAqMAk4804rnX-zkj9gi-HRSOVo54s8gGA3Wq04rslNwVggdRKj5JjBiyvyA9LL7vT3r7dKnVUvdWjetnFSZ1t33APRj8auDEIELcQgufjEtZFLf8JH4JMKAnb37w_WjF8G/s1600/Joseph's+Forgiveness+of+his+Brethren+By+Siegfried+Detler+Bendixen.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj0KqG4lDazRgAqMAk4804rnX-zkj9gi-HRSOVo54s8gGA3Wq04rslNwVggdRKj5JjBiyvyA9LL7vT3r7dKnVUvdWjetnFSZ1t33APRj8auDEIELcQgufjEtZFLf8JH4JMKAnb37w_WjF8G/s1600/Joseph's+Forgiveness+of+his+Brethren+By+Siegfried+Detler+Bendixen.jpg" width="257" /></a>On Yom Kippur, one is supposed to apologize for his wrongdoings, in front of God and in front of the people whom he may have wronged. In fact, when one apologizes before God, even his willful wrongdoings are considered mere mistakes. What is the proof? - from the phrase “Return… you have stumbled in your iniquity.” Iniquity is something done on purpose, yet here it is called “stumbled.” 
<br />
<br />
But we know more than that; his willful bad acts become his merits! What is the proof of that? - “And if a bad man turns away from his bad deeds… he shall live on account of them.” That is, even his bad deeds will provide merit for his future life. How can both be true? - the first applies when he apologizes out of fear, and the second - when he does it because of love.
<br />
<br />
Should one apologize again for something he apologized for last year? Some say he should not: he was already forgiven, and now he can only be sullied again by his memories. Others, however, say that it is even better, following the psalms, “I recognize my transgressions, and they are always in front of me.”
<br />
<br />
Art: Joseph's Forgiveness of his Brethren By Siegfried Detler Bendixen

---

**Source file:** `content/yoma/88.txt`

Yoma 88 – One should always forgive
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhv5XYcp3ARLFEUO4Xb8F94EjmgkU3hQefK8MU6PRTiHFuLVZDhrD3eesUWRhmQt6L8oFl4Jqw1gcjPHPXTl2W4D8ksbQOYmj1ZFa4ceBsg2G5f-qj_ue-Ofi-bdyrLKOUT2G0vzq7V2auL/s1600/Forgiven+by+Thomas+Faed.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="213" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhv5XYcp3ARLFEUO4Xb8F94EjmgkU3hQefK8MU6PRTiHFuLVZDhrD3eesUWRhmQt6L8oFl4Jqw1gcjPHPXTl2W4D8ksbQOYmj1ZFa4ceBsg2G5f-qj_ue-Ofi-bdyrLKOUT2G0vzq7V2auL/s1600/Forgiven+by+Thomas+Faed.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
Rav was explaining Torah verses in the class of his teacher, Rabbi Yehudah the Prince. Every time a new student came in, he was forced to start from the beginning, out of respect for him. Finally, when Rabbi Chanina came in, Rav did not restart, and Rabbi Chanina was offended. For thirteen years, Rav came to ask forgiveness on the eve of Yom Kippur, but Rabbi Chanina was not appeased.
<br />
<br />
How did Rav do it, seeing that one should not ask for forgiveness more than three times? - Rav went beyond the letter of the law. And how could Rabbi Chanina not forgive? We know that if one overlooks an insult and does not insist on his rights, then the Heavenly court overlooks his mistakes and the fact that he himself is unworthy? - Rabbi Chanina had a special reason: in a dream, he saw Rav hanging from a palm tree, and he knew that this meant that Rav was destined to become the head of the academy. This meant that he, Rabbi Chanina, who was the head of the academy in Israel, would have to die to vacate the post. Therefore, he pushed Rav to go to Babylonia, where Rav finally established his great academy, which existed for eight hundred years.
<br />
<br />
If one has a seminal emission on Yom Kippur, his sins are forgiven. But we learned in another place, “his sins are arranged in front of him!?” - Arranged to be forgiven.
<br />
<br />
Art: Forgiven by Thomas Faed

---

### content/yoma/9.txt

Yoma 9 – High Priesthood for sale
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgFUh2VteMjoaWIAiL7KqsmWCDBfsxqkPI25wxH_VUSC1-LnsfqBkSh5e7W0soeLTtRq4-UGHGe1h-jlaR9364gKi_V0MUPxSSxs7NfYLPTsbBt_sci-u-wuW6KStJg1HGyRu0zdwkrNCM4/s1600/Gossip+at+the+stile+By+Valentin+Walter+Bromley.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="238" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgFUh2VteMjoaWIAiL7KqsmWCDBfsxqkPI25wxH_VUSC1-LnsfqBkSh5e7W0soeLTtRq4-UGHGe1h-jlaR9364gKi_V0MUPxSSxs7NfYLPTsbBt_sci-u-wuW6KStJg1HGyRu0zdwkrNCM4/s320/Gossip+at+the+stile+By+Valentin+Walter+Bromley.jpg" width="320" /></a>At first, the chamber to which the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/11/yoma-2-staying-alone.html">High Priest was sequestered before Yom Kippur</a> was called “The chamber of the nobles,” but later, it became known as "The chamber of the administrators." This was because the High Priests of the first Temple were of greater stature. 
<br />
<br />
In fact, during the 410 years of the First Temple, there were a total of eighteen High Priests, which makes for 22 years in service on average. However, during the Second Temple, when they would buy High Priesthood with money, there were 300 of them during the 420 years of the Temple. If you subtract the forty years of service of Shimon the Righteous, eighty of Yochanan the Great, ten of Rabbi Ishmael, and eleven of Elazar ben Charsom, you will see that the majority of the High Priests did not live out one year of their service.
<br />
<br />
During the First Temple, bloodshed, immorality, and idol worship were abundant, yet only the Temple's roof was destroyed, and that only for seventy years. However, during the Second Temple, when ostensibly they were learning Torah and doing good deeds, the Temple was razed to the ground and is still not rebuilt. Why is that? – Because they slandered each other in secret and transgressed in secret. However, Resh Lakish presents another view: the later generations are greater because they still learn Torah with all the hardships.
<br />
<br />
Art: Gossip at the stile By Valentin Walter Bromley

---

### content/zevachim/10.txt
<a id="src-00304"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/10.txt`

Zevachim 10 – Thinking Ahead
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiI9g1DjEMJOqGxQjAtBtkKnqJMVb7GMdhEc372FmH1f7OW1IYwa5rpGOP_GIGikglMsPJp0cp2Fx88hlGztWQ3TNIQZ02d_UShRzgaTsa49vCc5-UwM0Kr3aeOXmXb9_Wk2ECb_jjpTD4/s1600/Camille+Pissarro+%253A+Flock+of+Sheep+in+a+Field+after+the+Harvest.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="252" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiI9g1DjEMJOqGxQjAtBtkKnqJMVb7GMdhEc372FmH1f7OW1IYwa5rpGOP_GIGikglMsPJp0cp2Fx88hlGztWQ3TNIQZ02d_UShRzgaTsa49vCc5-UwM0Kr3aeOXmXb9_Wk2ECb_jjpTD4/s320/Camille+Pissarro+%253A+Flock+of+Sheep+in+a+Field+after+the+Harvest.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">What happens if one slaughters an animal with the proper intent, that is, he knows what kind of sacrifice it is, but at the same time thinks that when doing the following step of the service - throwing the blood on the Altar - he will have the intention that it is a different type of sacrifice? What effect does this have on the sacrifice, even if he does not fulfill his intent later?<br />
<br />
Resh Lakish says that it is valid, but Rabbi Yochanan says that such a sacrifice is invalid. Rabbi Yochanan says that it is invalid, because he subscribes to the following principle: one can effectively “think ahead,” that is, that an intention that the kohen has for the following step of the service can affect what he is doing now. This result comes out because Rabbi Yochanan compares the intention that changes the type of sacrifice to the intention that changes its proper time or place, about which we will learn that it indeed disqualifies the offering. Resh Lakish holds that future intent does not count and considers the offering still valid.<br />
<br />
Art: Camille Pissarro : Flock of Sheep in a Field after the Harvest</span>

---

### content/zevachim/100.txt
<a id="src-00305"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/100.txt`

Zevachim 100 – Does the Mourner  Eat the Passover Sacrifice?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg-QuAnFlGd3v2scuxRrPqW8BFRviHdamlGef-yPER-DBB5nP9Z9CTya2EiqkOHDqdnn7SoOFCqMD7pO0SOAx-JaBUiPDhu600lyywmgty0axDVYIBWWoc_kU4vgeFz72ESPPhtY6PiWAc/s1600/Vasily+Perov+-+Seeing+off+the+Dead.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="257" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg-QuAnFlGd3v2scuxRrPqW8BFRviHdamlGef-yPER-DBB5nP9Z9CTya2EiqkOHDqdnn7SoOFCqMD7pO0SOAx-JaBUiPDhu600lyywmgty0axDVYIBWWoc_kU4vgeFz72ESPPhtY6PiWAc/s320/Vasily+Perov+-+Seeing+off+the+Dead.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Shimon made two statements in two different contexts, that the mourner can eat a Passover offering, and that he cannot. The Talmud gives five possible scenarios of how both can be true, one of them being offered by Abaye: one refers to a case when the mourner's relative died before midday, and the other – when he died after midday.<br />
<br />
If the relative died before midday when the mourner was not yet fit to offer a Passover sacrifice,  then the laws of mourning devolve on him first and prevent him from offering the sacrifice. If, however, the relative died after midday, the mourner was already obligated to bring the Passover sacrifice from before, and then the state of mourning does not prevent him from bringing the sacrifice.<br />
<br />
But do we find anywhere a difference between before and after midday? - Yes, we do! There was a story about a kohen named Yosef who did not want to become ritually impure because of his wife's burial, and the other kohanim forced him. On the other hand, the Torah tell the kohanim not to go into the cemetery, with the exception of burying his relatives? We have to say that one ruling applies after midday, while other one – before.<br />
<br />
Art: Vasily Perov - Seeing off the Dead</span>

---

### content/zevachim/101.txt
<a id="src-00306"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/101.txt`

Zevachim 101 – An Argument Between Moses and Aaron
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhOi537bfTMOEUjLmLRy6z2Klhe05TDwBUMY6Kwjoyp4M7H2HDomC75K-Z9HkNKCFmuBtes7JHZIFFbtr3MhbO6NVv2kkdKMifhs16XNBju-UZ7QBjKQE2soMR1w84UvtaeKYOj3UgmbtA/s1600/Johann+Hamza+-+A+Good+Dinner.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="254" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhOi537bfTMOEUjLmLRy6z2Klhe05TDwBUMY6Kwjoyp4M7H2HDomC75K-Z9HkNKCFmuBtes7JHZIFFbtr3MhbO6NVv2kkdKMifhs16XNBju-UZ7QBjKQE2soMR1w84UvtaeKYOj3UgmbtA/s320/Johann+Hamza+-+A+Good+Dinner.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">On the day when two of Aaron's sons died, Aaron with his remaining two sons did not eat the sacrifice of the New Moon but burned it instead. <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/10-17.htm">Moses began investigating why this happened</a>.<br />
<br />
He said “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/10-17.htm">Why did you not eat the sin-offering of New Moon?</a>” Moses asked Aaron, “Perhaps its blood was accidentally brought into the Most Holy chamber?” But Aaron replied, “Behold, it was not brought inside.”<br />
<br />
Moses then asked, “Perhaps it went outside the boundary,” but Aaron replied that it was always within. Moses then suggested, “Perhaps you offered it when you were mourners and thereby disqualified it?” - to which Aaron replied that he, the High Priest, has brought it, and the High Priest does not disqualify an offering even as a mourner. <br />
<br />
Having exhausted all possibilities, Moses demanded <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/10-18.htm">why it was not eaten, when they were commanded to do so</a>, and Aaron replied, “Today such things (as the death of my sons) happened, so perhaps you did not hear right what God has said, but eating should apply only <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/10-19.htm">to the inauguration sacrifices, and not the New Moon ones</a>.”<br />
<br />
Moses agreed completely and said, “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/10-20.htm">I heard it but forgot</a>.”<br />
<br />
Art: Johann Hamza - A Good Dinner</span>

---

### content/zevachim/102.txt
<a id="src-00307"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/102.txt`

Zevachim 102 – Was Moses a Kohen?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEga85BC90azaEmEsCc5s1MT9EbZVngHjQwoVSTr8PyKi-sLUE8Mi1mma6PT5zWqOOK0mskJk_O5xDLAU1jhiVMgJiiN1JXXU-oLZlJYWCaW914TOkwGDOw-VN_rDxU7mHiGXktamvWLaBo/s1600/Jules+Charles+Boquet+-+Mourning.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEga85BC90azaEmEsCc5s1MT9EbZVngHjQwoVSTr8PyKi-sLUE8Mi1mma6PT5zWqOOK0mskJk_O5xDLAU1jhiVMgJiiN1JXXU-oLZlJYWCaW914TOkwGDOw-VN_rDxU7mHiGXktamvWLaBo/s320/Jules+Charles+Boquet+-+Mourning.jpg" width="252" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav made the following statement: “Our teacher Moses was a High Priest and shared in the offerings – as the Torah says, '<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/8-29.htm">from the ram of inauguration was a portion of Moses</a>'”. Now he had to face the challenges.<br />
<br />
In the previous argument with Aaron about eating the sin-offering, why didn't Moses eat it himself, for he, unlike them, was not precluded by mourning? Rav answered – he was busy talking to God from morning till evening.<br />
<br />
When Miriam contracted leprosy, it was not Moses, who was not a kohen, who pronounced her status, and not Aaron, who was a relative, but it was God himself, who also was a kohen, Who confined her and later released her. We see from this that Moses was not a kohen!  - No, maybe leprosy is specifically given to the sons of Aaron to decide.<br />
<br />
In truth this is an&nbsp;</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">argument found</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">&nbsp;between earlier authorities of the Mishna, for when God became angry with Moses for refusing to go Egypt, this, unlike all other angers, left no mark – so says Rabbi Yehoshua ben Korcha. However, Rabbi Shimon says that this anger too left a mark, and Aaron became a kohen instead of Moses, who thus remained a Levi.<br />
<br />
Art: Jules Charles Boquet - Mourning</span>

---

### content/zevachim/103.txt

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/103.txt`

Zevachim 103 – Who Gets the Hide of a Sacrifice
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgqhfPqyCHxmvRfuFPJKnyWzf4lysgWam0_cD8Sm9f4n_2ck8GPaB81el-j9YzSgFLPgeoZi2_mQJ3jqoO1n5J0T-9gh3X8YVY7YL5tVGxXIfmVr2LzUfg4H4msqhH0nA2ln5HYNLnih64/s1600/Pieter+Gysels+-+Still+Life+with+Vegetables+Meat+Fruit+and+Game.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="219" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgqhfPqyCHxmvRfuFPJKnyWzf4lysgWam0_cD8Sm9f4n_2ck8GPaB81el-j9YzSgFLPgeoZi2_mQJ3jqoO1n5J0T-9gh3X8YVY7YL5tVGxXIfmVr2LzUfg4H4msqhH0nA2ln5HYNLnih64/s320/Pieter+Gysels+-+Still+Life+with+Vegetables+Meat+Fruit+and+Game.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The Torah states that <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/7-8.htm">the hide of a burnt offering is given to the kohanim</a>. However, this is true only if the offerings is valid; otherwise the meat is burned away from the Altar, and the hide is destroyed with it. <br />
<br />
Therefore, the rule is that whenever the Altar does not get the right to the meat, the kohanim do not get the right to the hide. However, if an offering was valid even for some time, so that the Altar got the right to the meat, the kohanim acquired the right to the hide. This rule is derived from a phrase “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/7-8.htm">the burnt offering of a man</a>.” Since the rule would be also true for a woman, the extra word “man” teaches us that it was valid for men to eat.<br />
<br />
Hides of regular offerings, such as a peace offering, belong to their owners. Hides of all most holy offerings other than the burnt offering also belong to the kohanim, and this is derived through logic: if in the case of a burnt offering, where the kohanim do not eat the meat, the hide nevertheless goes to them, then for a sin offering, where the kohanim do eat the meat, certainly the hide goes to them.<br />
<br />
Art: Pieter Gysels - Still Life with Vegetables Meat Fruit and Game</span>

---

Zevachim 104 – Hides of Invalidated Offerings
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi3CeO2bpAK3t3r2xPCrTvcETBUMkYFUlH713sL9OoR3JvP8X7gBtEoZJijj2ugNii7EEQSs-6GTC7yDMhU4M4ePuik4PA19aF5_VDwMmUS7OLXW46D5_dFHVPy4L98VmH0YLT9HDtQEWs/s1600/Giovacchino+Toma+-+The+Rain+Of+Ashes%252C+1880.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="198" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi3CeO2bpAK3t3r2xPCrTvcETBUMkYFUlH713sL9OoR3JvP8X7gBtEoZJijj2ugNii7EEQSs-6GTC7yDMhU4M4ePuik4PA19aF5_VDwMmUS7OLXW46D5_dFHVPy4L98VmH0YLT9HDtQEWs/s320/Giovacchino+Toma+-+The+Rain+Of+Ashes%252C+1880.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If an offering became invalidated prior to being skinned, its hide does not go to the kohanim. Only if the offering was skinned before it became invalidated, then the kohanim get the hide. Rabbi Chanina, the long-time administrator of the kohanim says, “In all the days of my life I never saw an invalidated hide being burned” - meaning that the invalidation discussed above never happened. But the Sages say that “I never saw” is not a proof. <br />
<br />
There are special sin-offerings, such as the goat brought for communal idol worship, that are not eaten but are burned in a designated place outside Jerusalem, called the place of ashes. These offerings contaminate the people who are carrying them, and they contaminate even the people's clothing. The offerings were carried out on poles. The first group of carriers becomes impure when it leaves the Courtyard, while the second group remains pure until they in their turn leave the Courtard. Rabbi Shimon says that none of them become impure until the fire catches onto the larger part of the sacrifice. <br />
<br />
Art: Giovacchino Toma - The Rain Of Ashes, 1880<br />
</span>

---

Zevachim 105 – The Impurity of Bulls and Goats that are Burned
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh2aT_2IG9pW-8egfnTN_U-9Vs3pr-uGIhYD6G9sTXvA6Af3ym_GjqBzYub8WOcbN3eOhglTPUQTHPoDAcoRDG_epwRrtoW3dCSWPwAgvNOZ0BLDSiuR250Of0e0JGMDkDnzW_IsnuEWPU/s1600/Henri+De+Toulouse-Lautrec+-+Two+Bulls+Wearing+a+Yoke.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="237" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh2aT_2IG9pW-8egfnTN_U-9Vs3pr-uGIhYD6G9sTXvA6Af3ym_GjqBzYub8WOcbN3eOhglTPUQTHPoDAcoRDG_epwRrtoW3dCSWPwAgvNOZ0BLDSiuR250Of0e0JGMDkDnzW_IsnuEWPU/s320/Henri+De+Toulouse-Lautrec+-+Two+Bulls+Wearing+a+Yoke.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Elazar asked the following question, “If exactly half of the carcass of a bull or a goat that are burned has left the Courtyard, together with the majority of one of its limb, is the remaining part of that limb considered outside, together with the limb? Or perhaps, since the limb belongs to the body, and the body is only half-out, then the limb is considered inside?” To this there was no answer.<br />
<br />
Some say that Rabbi Eliezer asked a different question: “If three of the five carriers have left the Courtyard, are the other two carriers&nbsp;</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">considered&nbsp;</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">already out and impure?” To this there was also no answer.</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;"> <br />
Rabbi Elazar asked another question, “Do the bulls that are burned&nbsp;</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">already</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">&nbsp;contaminate foods and liquids while they are still inside the Courtyard?” Since they will have a very strong impurity when they are out of the Courtyard,&nbsp;perhaps&nbsp;it is enough to make food and liquids impure, since these are easily rendered impure. Afterwards he himself resolved it: prior to their exiting from the Courtyard they are not fully considered bulls that are burned, and thus they do not contaminate the food yet.”<br />
<br />
Art: Henri De Toulouse-Lautrec - Two Bulls Wearing a Yoke</span>

Zevachim 106 – Sacrifices Outside the Temple
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhDuld0m4fA7YYPYKwBAwLHaBg85sBIOXROpqW-346Lbg_nfPsxskS8ogVGSln4INbzRNlM1vPf4fQmmqxy4-L2huojGsrH36veJZAg3q6O7ocI8aVIIB1aGMLIpWtjj5odqbLE1UYhPBM/s1600/Abel+Grimmer+-+A+Wooded+Winter+Village+Landscape+With+Peasants+Slaughtering.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="226" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhDuld0m4fA7YYPYKwBAwLHaBg85sBIOXROpqW-346Lbg_nfPsxskS8ogVGSln4INbzRNlM1vPf4fQmmqxy4-L2huojGsrH36veJZAg3q6O7ocI8aVIIB1aGMLIpWtjj5odqbLE1UYhPBM/s320/Abel+Grimmer+-+A+Wooded+Winter+Village+Landscape+With+Peasants+Slaughtering.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">It is forbidden to slaughter and to burn sacrifices outside the Temple. What happens when one transgresses this prohibition? <br />
<br />
If one slaughtered and burned a sacrifice outside the Temple, he is liable for slaughtering it, and he is liable for burning it as well. Rabbi Yose HaGlili says: “If he slaughtered the sacrifices inside the Temple, so that it was indeed valid, and then burned it outside, then he is liable for burning. But if he slaughtered it outside, then it became invalid right away, and he is not liable if he then burns it.”  <br />
<br />
But the Sages told him, “Even in your case, when he slaughtered the sacrifice inside the Temple, it becomes invalid as soon as he takes it out. Then he should not be liable for burning it outside! According to your logic, Rabbi Yose, one should never be liable for burning an offering outside. This proves that you are wrong, and that when one slaughtered and burned an offering outside the Temple, he is liable for both acts.<br />
<br />
Challenge: what can Rabbi Yose answer in his defense?<br />
<br />
Art: Abel Grimmer - A Wooded Winter Village Landscape With Peasants Slaughtering</span>

---

### content/zevachim/107.txt
<a id="src-00312"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/107.txt`

Zevachim 107 – What does “Outside” Mean
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiP8si_HljnDAB6dcxpF4VZ2DrgK3Pwf8y15wWvJpkV4WBFM7vFFUmmm64_GMNE63ca-ZrwFr-513raztzIChbvvggW6mEHlQ0MHlVF1c95Dxs6V7LcXGX6ozBrNUi4Q0AVD-prw8N_sT8/s1600/Cornelis+van+Leemputten+-+Shepherdess+with+Sheep+in+a+Landscape.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="213" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiP8si_HljnDAB6dcxpF4VZ2DrgK3Pwf8y15wWvJpkV4WBFM7vFFUmmm64_GMNE63ca-ZrwFr-513raztzIChbvvggW6mEHlQ0MHlVF1c95Dxs6V7LcXGX6ozBrNUi4Q0AVD-prw8N_sT8/s320/Cornelis+van+Leemputten+-+Shepherdess+with+Sheep+in+a+Landscape.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who offers sacrifices outside the Temple is liable, but what does “outside the Temple” mean?<br />
<br />
The verse states, “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/17-3.htm">And any man from the House of Israel who will slaughter an ox, a sheep or goat in the camp... and he did not bring it to the Tent of the Meeting</a>... ” &nbsp;We might think that even if he takes a sacrifice that is normally brought in the northern part of the Courtyard and slaughters it in the southern part of the Courtyard – he would already be liable.  To dispel this notion, the Torah added, “outside the camp.”<br />
<br />
But now that the Torah has said, “outside the camp,” you might think this to mean outside of all three special camps, that is, outside the Temple, outside the Temple Mount, and even outside Jerusalem – that only then one would be liable. For that, the Torah said, “in the camp.” Thus, if he slaughters a sacrifices in the south, even if it is not its place, it is not called “outside,” because some other sacrifices can be brought there. However, if he slaughters it outside the Courtyard, then he is liable for “slaughter outside.”<br />
<br />
Art: Cornelis van Leemputten - Shepherdess with Sheep in a Landscape</span>

---

### content/zevachim/108.txt
<a id="src-00313"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/108.txt`

Zevachim 108 - Stringencies of Slaughtering and of Offering Up a Sacrifice Outside
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi3VJB8orvUTilAxsnjGmRRggx1l4FFErZL4SdAbgJQCLmzUECVbT_Dk-FkYU-FJ4aGbpGvhjNuLpEGYuSoCs4-docBQU6rDNcmAqROey1bb_M41Y5QK64MOYZK_UZSAQlsMtnEyrB3eNs/s1600/William+Lucas+-+Sharpening+The+Knife+1868.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi3VJB8orvUTilAxsnjGmRRggx1l4FFErZL4SdAbgJQCLmzUECVbT_Dk-FkYU-FJ4aGbpGvhjNuLpEGYuSoCs4-docBQU6rDNcmAqROey1bb_M41Y5QK64MOYZK_UZSAQlsMtnEyrB3eNs/s320/William+Lucas+-+Sharpening+The+Knife+1868.jpg" width="276" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">There are ways in which slaughtering a sacrifice outside the Temple is more stringent, and there are other ways in which offering it up (burning) are more stringent.<br />
<br />
If one takes an animal that was consecrated as a sacrifice and slaughters it for someone's consumption, he is liable to slaughtering outside. If, however, he offers it up for someone, he is not liable for offering up a sacrifice outside the Temple, because he did not dedicate it to God. In truth, he is liable for idol worship for&nbsp;worshiping&nbsp;that human, but that is a different liability.<br />
<br />
Offering up is more stringent in this way: if two people held a knife together and slaughtered a sacrifice outside the Temple, they are not liable, but if they took a sacrificial limb and offered it up, they are liable.<br />
<br />
If one offered a limb of a sacrifice, then became aware that it was prohibited, then forgot it, then offered another limb, again became aware and again forgot it, and so on, he is liable for each limb – so says Rabbi Shimon, but Rabbi Yose makes him liable just once.<br />
<br />
Art: William Lucas - Sharpening The Knife 1868<br />
</span>

---

### content/zevachim/109.txt
<a id="src-00314"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/109.txt`

Zevachim 109 – Does One Need an Altar to Sacrifice Outside?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi_8BnISJ8zoYTJCE7AjYPJIdn7_1SXPWeW66-4pzVl3g3GIoXfOkdOED2-0b-kMKcSSg3GPzcXF4Jn62yeqGyW9rE10YGTmCUi3DUGALU6frRvsOGNSUgVrb5Q12bRRpsk7PPRnQgMnFM/s1600/Adam+Colonia+-+Noah+Leaving+the+Ark.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="310" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi_8BnISJ8zoYTJCE7AjYPJIdn7_1SXPWeW66-4pzVl3g3GIoXfOkdOED2-0b-kMKcSSg3GPzcXF4Jn62yeqGyW9rE10YGTmCUi3DUGALU6frRvsOGNSUgVrb5Q12bRRpsk7PPRnQgMnFM/s320/Adam+Colonia+-+Noah+Leaving+the+Ark.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">According to Rabbi Yose, one is not liable for offering up outside, unless he offers the sacrifice upon the top of an altar, but Rabbi Shimon says, “Even if he offered up on a rock or on a stone he is liable.”<br />
<br />
What is Rabbi Yose's reason? - It is written, “<a href="http://bible.cc/genesis/8-20.htm">and Noah built an altar to God</a>” - which proves that an altar is required. And what is the reason of Rabbi Shimon? - It is written, “<a href="http://bible.cc/judges/13-19.htm">And Manoach took the goat-kid and the flour offering and he offered them up on the rock to God.</a>”<br />
<br />
How does Rabbi Shimon explain Noah's altar? - He says it was built only to provide comfortable height upon which to perform the sacrifice. And how does Rabbi Yose explain the rock of Manoach? - An angel told Manoach to act thus.<br />
<br />
For what sacrifices is one liable when offering them outside? - Any valid sacrifice, or even an invalid one if it would be accepted on the Altar after the fact. One is liable for offering an olive's volume of the meat, flour, and incense. For non-blood offerings, Rabbi Elazar makes him liable only for a complete amount.<br />
<br />
Art: Adam Colonia - Noah Leaving the Ark</span>

---

### content/zevachim/11.txt
<a id="src-00315"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/11.txt`

Zevachim 11 – The Common Side Logic
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiYcdqM8eDKHaccCu-wVT2rUNhfJfQ2wXlOCusONFA7jnEFS5iofIYO65SDPqHO2byWqiOARmCln80-1FKwUHWbWJ20FyWdM5T43Y8_wiw0pea5asvppceMGtqhyt6FGdzW-9hv4tsZWmo/s1600/Abraham+Solomon+-+Not+Guilty+%2528The+Acquittal%2529.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="254" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiYcdqM8eDKHaccCu-wVT2rUNhfJfQ2wXlOCusONFA7jnEFS5iofIYO65SDPqHO2byWqiOARmCln80-1FKwUHWbWJ20FyWdM5T43Y8_wiw0pea5asvppceMGtqhyt6FGdzW-9hv4tsZWmo/s320/Abraham+Solomon+-+Not+Guilty+%2528The+Acquittal%2529.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Most sacrifices are brought in the Temple courtyard at the Altar, but  not inside the Sanctuary proper. In fact, the Torah says that “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/6-30.htm">Any sin-offering whose blood was brought into the Tent of Meeting... may not be eaten</a>.” Rabbi Eliezer says that this is also true of the guilt-offering, since the Torah said, “just as the guilt-offering so is the sin-offering,” but the Sages insist that this is only true for the sin-offering.<br />
<br />
What is the reason of the Sages - for seemingly, the Torah supports Rabbi Eliezer? The Sages defend with this logic: if burnt offering, which is completely burnt, is not disqualified by bringing its blood inside the Temple, then the guilt-offering, which is not completely burnt, surely cannot be thus  disqualified! Now the arguments are as follows:<br />
<br />
* burnt offering is no proof, because it does not achieve atonement!<br />
* but the flour of a the one who swore falsely achieves atonement and still it is not disqualified if part of it is brought inside!<br />
* but the flour does not require slaughter!<br />
* but burnt offering does require slaughter and is not disqualified!<br />
<br />
We came a full circle. What is common between all these? That they are holy and are not disqualified by bringing their blood inside, so the guilt-offering is not disqualified – say the Sages.<br />
<br />
Art: Abraham Solomon - Not Guilty (The Acquittal)<br />
</span>

---

### content/zevachim/110.txt
<a id="src-00316"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/110.txt`

Zevachim 110 – Offering Parts of Sacrifices Outside
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjamrimgv4RjiOPNnoK2mvqjDQ0icJD71lJjMVto4ejr9n-RrHnIv4IvLH5K4i2a4VtzpAeifXAeHAUZ2uQdY4NhaM0KUwmFAh3bYMCuMA1ei6DoxaUUTkzC8i8C5wzHysI2DxO-a0_VGQ/s1600/Gerrit+Dou+-+Woman+Pouring+Water+Into+A+Jar.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjamrimgv4RjiOPNnoK2mvqjDQ0icJD71lJjMVto4ejr9n-RrHnIv4IvLH5K4i2a4VtzpAeifXAeHAUZ2uQdY4NhaM0KUwmFAh3bYMCuMA1ei6DoxaUUTkzC8i8C5wzHysI2DxO-a0_VGQ/s320/Gerrit+Dou+-+Woman+Pouring+Water+Into+A+Jar.jpg" width="249" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A flour offering includes flour, oil, and frankincense. A handful of flour is separated first and burned on the Altar, and then the remainder is eaten by the Kohanim. If one burned this remainder as an offering outside the Temple, he is not liable, because the remainder was not destined for the Altar. If, however, he mixed the handful back in and burned the mixture outside – he is liable, because after all the handful has been burned.<br />
<br />
If one throws a part of the sacrificial blood upon an altar outside the Temple, he is liable. On Sukkot, they poured pure water on the Altar, in addition to wine, and Rabbi Elazar says that for puring this water outside one is also liable. Rabbi Nechemia makes one liable even for pouring the remnants of the blood of the offering, since the remnants are supposed to go to the base of the Altar.<br />
<br />
Art: Gerrit Dou - Woman Pouring Water Into A Jar<br />
</span>

---

### content/zevachim/111.txt
<a id="src-00317"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/111.txt`

Zevachim 111 – Sacrificing Birds Outside the Temple
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXtbTW4jkPweFUoCTvfQH7TCp0A38QPpp0w6fOs8A0G1cF8BLy9NexRQKcDFUuxblDhyN06NxXPSijQGiQLiH0TdVLB9mCCcytLNGbvLOumgHA20HCv5Urip5e1LEKkslY2eDZTw1EVU4/s1600/Perrault+Leon+Jean+Basile+-+The+Bird+Charmer+1873.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXtbTW4jkPweFUoCTvfQH7TCp0A38QPpp0w6fOs8A0G1cF8BLy9NexRQKcDFUuxblDhyN06NxXPSijQGiQLiH0TdVLB9mCCcytLNGbvLOumgHA20HCv5Urip5e1LEKkslY2eDZTw1EVU4/s320/Perrault+Leon+Jean+Basile+-+The+Bird+Charmer+1873.jpg" width="261" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one performed proper killing (</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/01/zevachim-68-when-is-bird-considered.html">melikah</a>,&nbsp;</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">when its head is severed from the nape</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">)&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: medium;">of the bird</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">,&nbsp;</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">and he did it in the Temple, and then offered that bird outside, he is liable, because with melikah the bird becomes fit for the Altar. However, if he performed melikah outside, he is not liable either for that, or for bringing it up. Melikah way of killing outside the Temple is not proper, and it makes the bird unfit for consumption and invalid as a sacrifice.</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;"> <br />
If he performed regular kosher slaughter of the bird with a knife and offered it up – he is, contrary to the expectations, liable, because of an additional phrase “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/17-3.htm">or who will slaughter</a>.”<br />
<br />
We thus find that what makes the bird a valid sacrifice (melikah) inside  makes one not liable if done outside, and what makes one liable (shechitah, or kosher slaughter) outside makes one not liable if done inside.<br />
<br />
Art: Perrault Leon Jean Basile - The Bird Charmer 1873</span>

---

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/112.txt`

Zevachim 112 – When One is not Liable for Sacrificing Outside
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh7F6O5Sxd8Z-cieFTWKG6ufvMQcLaEwZ6qSt7YPZ2mGHfj-ueR0UrQTgFFEaQQNpcbM6_lN9Vd3eEK7AM3DsRsZRbh5Sfv2tuDB6BtJGZaQQhiaP2y4X5AD-2_rIjjt4NOyqSUOAcFyN0/s1600/Van+Gogh+-+Cows+after+Jordaens.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="254" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh7F6O5Sxd8Z-cieFTWKG6ufvMQcLaEwZ6qSt7YPZ2mGHfj-ueR0UrQTgFFEaQQNpcbM6_lN9Vd3eEK7AM3DsRsZRbh5Sfv2tuDB6BtJGZaQQhiaP2y4X5AD-2_rIjjt4NOyqSUOAcFyN0/s320/Van+Gogh+-+Cows+after+Jordaens.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A Red Heifer is a cow that is slaughtered east of Jerusalem on the Mount of Olives and is burned in a special pit excavated for this purpose. Its ashes, mixed with spring water, are used to purify people from ritual contamination caused by a corpse. If one sacrifices this cow as an offering outside the Temple, he is not liable, because the phrase “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/17-4.htm">and to the entrance of the Tent of the Meeting he did not bring it</a>” does not apply to it. In the same way the scapegoat that is sent away on Yom Kippur does not entail liability if sacrificed outside.<br />
<br />
Other animals do not entail liability for sacrificing outside because they are cannot be brought “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/17-4.htm">as an offering before God</a>.” This list includes an animal that has sodomized a person or was sodomized by a man, one designated as idolatrous sacrifice or one that was worshipped, one that was used as dog's exchange or a harlot's payment, torn by a wild beast, or born by Caesarean section.<br />
<br />
Art: Van Gogh - Cows after Jordaens</span>

---

Zevachim 113 – Was There Flood in the Land of Israel?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjP-VLCDjurQbNEnej8XrAomw7DBD48349jIMqCY_WQD7pmWQqsxxOQdlCk-_K8oUocVpyB2HQy9VCJB7LOvBPKbWG3A1xBjjz7FUY-RO4p_XXPSlRvmifFoCJoyIs-yFP2Dm_zu3pLdg0/s1600/Bonaventura%252C+the+Elder+Peeters+-+The+Great+Flood.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="174" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjP-VLCDjurQbNEnej8XrAomw7DBD48349jIMqCY_WQD7pmWQqsxxOQdlCk-_K8oUocVpyB2HQy9VCJB7LOvBPKbWG3A1xBjjz7FUY-RO4p_XXPSlRvmifFoCJoyIs-yFP2Dm_zu3pLdg0/s320/Bonaventura%252C+the+Elder+Peeters+-+The+Great+Flood.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The red heifer was burned in a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/03/zevachim-112-when-one-is-not-liable-for.html">pit specially excavated for it</a>, but what does this mean? Resh Lakish says that it was pre-inspected to be free of corpse impurity, but Rabbi Yochanan says that it simply means that it was outside the walls of Jerusalem.<br />
<br />
The root of their argument is the question whether the Flood extended to the Land of Israel. According to Resh Lakish, it did, and therefore there were remains of people embedded in the earth. According to Rabbi Yochanan, the Flood did not visit Israel, and people's remains were not a concern.<br />
<br />
But did not Nebuchadnezzar also kill Jews? - Their remains were cleared away, says Rabbi Yochanan. And Resh Lakish? He says that they were cleared away from Jerusalem, but not outside.<br />
<br />
But if the Flood did cover Israel, how did the gigantic sheep called Re'em survive? According to Rabbi Yochanan, all is well, and the Re'em stood in Israel. Says Resh Lakish, Re'em was then a young cub! But Rabbah bar bar Chanah saw a cub of a Re'em, and it was like a mount Tabor! Says Resh Lakish – his nostril fit inside the Arc.<br />
<br />
Art: Bonaventura, the Elder Peeters - The Great Flood</span>

---

Zevachim 114 – Temporarily Blemished Sacrifices Brought Outside
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiQytzkHzli2Er3D0u5MqPR3X99_WhK8g59hhgTs7rOIyK4ouz28STbg8Ru573NpTIuWq_jcDK5Hc9t9C1u2ZC8qqkt6krdPpBgU1Y0A3ldkE6sFIIh8Y3LxWEtkKLmZpcW9DFCXJMQmu4/s1600/Giovanni+Segantini+-+Il+reddito+del+pastore.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="212" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiQytzkHzli2Er3D0u5MqPR3X99_WhK8g59hhgTs7rOIyK4ouz28STbg8Ru573NpTIuWq_jcDK5Hc9t9C1u2ZC8qqkt6krdPpBgU1Y0A3ldkE6sFIIh8Y3LxWEtkKLmZpcW9DFCXJMQmu4/s320/Giovanni+Segantini+-+Il+reddito+del+pastore.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a sacrifice has a permanent blemish, then it cannot be brought “before God,” and therefore everybody  agrees that one who sacrifices it outside the Temple is not liable. However, if one sacrifices an animal with a temporarily blemish, then Rabbi Shimon says that he violates a negative commandment and is liable to lashes, but the Sages consider him completely exempt.<br />
<br />
The reason of the Sages is clear – a temporarily blemished animal cannot be currently brought “before God,” but what is the reason of Rabbi Shimon? - He bases his opinion on the phrase, “<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/12-8.htm">You shall not do everything we do today, each man what is proper in his eyes</a>.” The word “proper” means “proper in the eyes of the man who offers” now, and will become so in the eyes of God later - and it is this action that "you shall not do."<br />
<br />
Art: Giovanni Segantini - Il reddito del pastore</span>

---
