Zevachim 115 – When Sacrificing Outside is Permitted
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjE8FHDURlmDu61-zi4Q6AgbSJJBeUnMomffDXJNzsX6aTPSp8J5dggoDdcuQY8sDyJX8lfI8wYSnjp3hA6txkq1kWXLIS-CUVWmm76zjpTf2GsJnJp_bHyzCk7k7Yw4QnNZw1tFq9n3Zk/s1600/Johann+Wilhelm+Schirmer+-+The+Departure+Of+The+Man+To+Jericho+Morning+C.1856.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="231" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjE8FHDURlmDu61-zi4Q6AgbSJJBeUnMomffDXJNzsX6aTPSp8J5dggoDdcuQY8sDyJX8lfI8wYSnjp3hA6txkq1kWXLIS-CUVWmm76zjpTf2GsJnJp_bHyzCk7k7Yw4QnNZw1tFq9n3Zk/s320/Johann+Wilhelm+Schirmer+-+The+Departure+Of+The+Man+To+Jericho+Morning+C.1856.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One is not liable for burning outside those parts of the sacrifices that are eaten and do not go on the Altar. One is also not liable for actions that are not the last step in the service, thus, for example, one is not liable for separating a handful from the flour-offering, but is liable for burning it. Likewise, one is not liable for receiving the blood, but is liable for throwing it on the altar.<br />
<br />
Initially sacrificial service was done by the firstborn, and everybody was allowed to build his private altar. This is mentioned in the Torah when it says, “<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/24-5.htm">And Moses sent the youths of the Children of Israel, and they brought up burnt offerings</a>.” The firstborn lost this privilege after they worshipped the Golden Calf, and the kohanim, the sons of Aaron, began to serve in their stead.<br />
<br />
Once the Tabernacle was erected, private altars became forbidden. When the Jews came Israel, crossed the Jordan, and erected the Tabernacle at Gilgal, near Jericho, private altars again became permitted. F</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">inally, t</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">hey became completely prohibited after the building of the Temple in Jerusalem.<br />
<br />
Art: Johann Wilhelm Schirmer - The Departure Of The Man To Jericho Morning C.1856</span>

---

Zevachim 116 –  How to Bring Sacrifices on a Private Altar
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh9TzI1CJ7UM8ELUhtcza5ZoBXeteMLPlAmdusfD6WaZLM3hTO06nSjiogzGX3u-m9zu874cQUPzbKVqW47vJOS4MVVN3pH5scEhyphenhyphenhxggbT_fpvmSJBRy_qnuVbh9t8-o8KP9BLieq2UQw/s1600/Lovis+%2528Franz+Heinrich+Louis%2529+Corinth+-+The+Painter+Charlotte+Berend+With+A+Bull+1902.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="229" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh9TzI1CJ7UM8ELUhtcza5ZoBXeteMLPlAmdusfD6WaZLM3hTO06nSjiogzGX3u-m9zu874cQUPzbKVqW47vJOS4MVVN3pH5scEhyphenhyphenhxggbT_fpvmSJBRy_qnuVbh9t8-o8KP9BLieq2UQw/s320/Lovis+%2528Franz+Heinrich+Louis%2529+Corinth+-+The+Painter+Charlotte+Berend+With+A+Bull+1902.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When private altars were allowed, one could bring any clean (kosher) animal: domesticated, wild, or a bird, provided that it was not missing a complete limb. This was still permitted to non-Jews after the Temple was built and the Jews had to bring their sacrifices there.<br />
<br />
Could the sacrifices brought on private altar be eaten as peace-offerings, or did they have to be burned, as burnt-offerings? Those who say that they could be eaten point out that “<a href="http://bible.cc/genesis/4-4.htm">Abel brought from the firstlings of his flock and from their fats</a>...” - that is, he brought the fats but ate the rest. And those who say that Abel brought only burnt-offerings explain that he brought the fattest of the lambs and burned them completely.<br />
<br />
But didn't <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/18-12.htm">Jethro bring peace-offerings</a>? – Jethro came after the giving of the Torah, when eating sacrifices became allowed.<br />
<br />
What did Jethro <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/18-1.htm">hear that he came</a>? He heard about the splitting of the Red Sea. But why did Rahav say about it “<a href="http://bible.cc/joshua/2-11.htm">No spirit remained <i>erect</i> in any man</a>” (hint)? – She knew, because there was no leader or ruler who did not come to her. She started at 10, was a prostitute for 40 years, and converted at 50.<br />
<br />
Art: Lovis (Franz Heinrich Louis) Corinth - The Painter Charlotte Berend With A Bull 1902<br />
</span>

---

### content/zevachim/117.txt

Zevachim 117 – The Three Camps
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjfebwU00Lsdr30MA4Yj11zp_gZJRAhUPaTLVAJyqukVx0PD5rrMQx2tCtO15uTuIzNe9P2Oo9dj2z-3boVLRNvY4d5htvnUbcuP7wl8xnGSxChm_L6g_tiUMSET4IeYMRG48Pg5e2xeTc/s1600/Eug%25C3%25A8ne-Alexis+Girardet+-+Bedouins+In+The+Desert.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="198" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjfebwU00Lsdr30MA4Yj11zp_gZJRAhUPaTLVAJyqukVx0PD5rrMQx2tCtO15uTuIzNe9P2Oo9dj2z-3boVLRNvY4d5htvnUbcuP7wl8xnGSxChm_L6g_tiUMSET4IeYMRG48Pg5e2xeTc/s320/Eug%25C3%25A8ne-Alexis+Girardet+-+Bedouins+In+The+Desert.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When the Jews lived in the desert, their encampment was divided into three areas: the Tabernacle, or the Camp of the Divine Presence, the Levite Camp, and the Israelite camp. Corresponding to these, in the times of the Temple there were the Temple, the Temple Mount, and Jerusalem. <br />
<br />
Each area had its laws. A Metzora (spiritual leper) may not enter the Israelite camp, that is, Jerusalem at the time of the Temple, and the encampment at the time of the desert. An accidental murder was exiled to the Levite Camp, and in the time of the Temple, to one of the cities where the Levites lived. If a Levi murdered by accident, he had to be exiled to another Levite city, but if we moved from one neighborhood to another, this was sufficient. One who was ritually impure because of contact with a dead body could enter the Levite Camp (Temple Mount), but not the Temple proper.<br />
<br />
Art: Eugène-Alexis Girardet - Bedouins In The Desert</span>

---

### content/zevachim/118.txt
<a id="src-00324"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/118.txt`

Zevachim 118 – How Long Did the Tabernacle Stand?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh1QtKxBU4HitoOjf9UgVKwEvhpNF9GHwVcvGHrxmQHs1k5wu5xop2cOifSRnCZG5aas0KMKOQ3wvp0oaFnd4eswkQxwKYCTtzv2-NSLRczby3hX8UiVbjkhbKXcQQFJp4CODrdwx-TyPM/s1600/Frederic+Edwin+Church+-+Twilight+In+The+Wilderness.jpeg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="198" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh1QtKxBU4HitoOjf9UgVKwEvhpNF9GHwVcvGHrxmQHs1k5wu5xop2cOifSRnCZG5aas0KMKOQ3wvp0oaFnd4eswkQxwKYCTtzv2-NSLRczby3hX8UiVbjkhbKXcQQFJp4CODrdwx-TyPM/s320/Frederic+Edwin+Church+-+Twilight+In+The+Wilderness.jpeg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The days of the Tent of Meeting in the wilderness were forty years minus one, that is, thirty-nine: in the first year following the Exodus from Egypt Moses built the Tabernacle, in the second year it was erected, and then Moses sent out the spies, which led to a 40-year stay in the desert.<br />
<br />
The days of the Tent of Meeting at Gilgal numbered 14 years: 7 during the conquest of the Land of Israel, and 7 years while the land was divided. We know this from the life of Calev, who was 40 when the spies were sent out, 78 when they crossed the Jordan, and 85 when the land was conquered. Since the land was being conquered for 7 years, we can assume that it was also divided for 7 years.<br />
<br />
The Tabernacle then stood in Shiloh for 369 years. In Nov and Giveon it stood for another 57 years, moving between these two places - and we know this from the lives of Eli the Priest and Samuel - until the Temple was built. <br />
<br />
Art: Frederic Edwin Church - Twilight In The Wilderness</span>

---

### content/zevachim/119.txt
<a id="src-00325"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/119.txt`

Zevachim 119 – The Resting Place and the Inheritance
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZBpm-Fic6DgmLa9U76RIWw4Sl74AfQJVsVXQvTHCxUgno5IcPvZXLYANgFDOz5VDIpiVFEPk4QMLTLjUH4p9a6iXJEUJYCtfI01fZsMTC5tCxaQIKdYdxwMLXFbw9_GXtIH6NRHwJnfk/s1600/John+William+Waterhouse+-+A+Roman+Offering.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="400" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZBpm-Fic6DgmLa9U76RIWw4Sl74AfQJVsVXQvTHCxUgno5IcPvZXLYANgFDOz5VDIpiVFEPk4QMLTLjUH4p9a6iXJEUJYCtfI01fZsMTC5tCxaQIKdYdxwMLXFbw9_GXtIH6NRHwJnfk/s400/John+William+Waterhouse+-+A+Roman+Offering.jpg" width="146" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Moses said that there will be periods when private altars will be permitted, “<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/12-9.htm">for you have not yet come to the resting place or to the inheritance</a>.” The “resting place” refers to Shiloh, and “the inheritance” refers to Jerusalem. When the Tabernacle stood either in Shiloh or Jerusalem, private altars were forbidden. However, before that, at Gilgal, and between these time period, when it stood in Nov and Giveon, private altars were permitted.<br />
<br />
According to Rabbi Yishmael, both “resting place” and “inheritance” refer to Shiloh, and no verse is needed to teach that private altars were permitted in between, because we find many righteous individual using them. According to Rabbi Shimon, both refer to Jerusalem, and private altars were always permitted before then.<br />
<br />
Private altar does not require leaning on the sacrifice, or the northern side of the altar, or application of blood all around the altar, or waving the offering, or bringing the flour offering to the southern corner of the altar. Rabbi Yehudah says that there are no flour offerings on a private altar.<br />
<br />
Art: John William Waterhouse - A Roman Offering</span>

---

### content/zevachim/12.txt
<a id="src-00326"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/12.txt`

Zevachim 12 – Rushing with the Passover Sacrifice
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjHBcBT6hn1BXXudlUDvO85zSFYgkLOZwF0i_VWmICqdVlHUELzeSIHJCfIfCE2tUBux8FBYNGIGE7bO7M8e89yoCpBGB1n_k_wfC6sK9G-PkIcgo8J0jvnbAofigSE-Bss757RYrAAjXM/s1600/Jacopo+d%2527Antonio+Negretti+-+Passover.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="185" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjHBcBT6hn1BXXudlUDvO85zSFYgkLOZwF0i_VWmICqdVlHUELzeSIHJCfIfCE2tUBux8FBYNGIGE7bO7M8e89yoCpBGB1n_k_wfC6sK9G-PkIcgo8J0jvnbAofigSE-Bss757RYrAAjXM/s320/Jacopo+d%2527Antonio+Negretti+-+Passover.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A Passover offering should be brought in the afternoon of the fourteenth of Nissan, for its sake. Bringing it as any other sacrifice makes it completely invalid.<br />
<br />
What happens if one changed two of these conditions: he brought it early, in the morning of the fourteenth, and for the sake of a different sacrifice (one can imagine that he rushed early in the morning, but then realized that it was too early and decided to bring it as a peace-offering).<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yehoshua considers this as if he brought it on the thirteenth, and as any Passover sacrifice brought outside its time as a different one, it is valid. Ben Beteira says that morning is like afternoon, and the sacrifice is invalid.<br />
<br />
Ben Azzai goes back to the </span><span style="font-size: medium;"> very first ruling of this Tractate and&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: medium;"> disagrees with it, saying, based on a tradition from the seventy-two members of the Sanhedrin,  that sacrifices that are eaten, if brought for a different type, are valid. This rule adds only the burnt offering to the invalid ones, but the Sages did not agree with him.<br />
<br />
Art: Jacopo d'Antonio Negretti - Passover</span>

---

### content/zevachim/120.txt
<a id="src-00327"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/120.txt`

Zevachim 120 – Not Everything is Allowed on a Private Altar
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgUWiBjt-_7mAvXmpIJWIb5Gtcd222OZwgbnZd-hbFcGP-5QSCojefrHfhgIyYMocIGGqYtBQQQ5Nf8yh-InD2HzYK8p2rnuSP6YbGd_3iuoXO16JULNtNlQutx4zgx6smokSHdowAyQec/s1600/Frans+Snyders+-+Concert+of+Birds.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="159" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgUWiBjt-_7mAvXmpIJWIb5Gtcd222OZwgbnZd-hbFcGP-5QSCojefrHfhgIyYMocIGGqYtBQQQ5Nf8yh-InD2HzYK8p2rnuSP6YbGd_3iuoXO16JULNtNlQutx4zgx6smokSHdowAyQec/s320/Frans+Snyders+-+Concert+of+Birds.png" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">There are <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/03/zevachim-116-how-to-bring-sacrifices-on.html">many aspects in which the sacrificial service in the Temple in Jerusalem is stricter than that of the private altar</a>. However, there are three aspect in which they are the same. <br />
<br />
One is liable for the following on a private altar: if he eats the sacrifice beyond the allowed time; if one had a wrong intent to eat the sacrifice beyond allowed time, the sacrifice becomes invalid and one is liable for eating it; one is liable for eating it while being ritually impure.<br />
<br />
How do we know that? In fact, we might even think the opposite. The Torah stated <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/7-17.htm">that a sacrifice kept overnight is burned and one that goes out of the Temple is also burned</a>. &nbsp;Therefore I might think that since the sacrifice on the private altar already exited the Temple and was not burned, so too one that was left overnight is not burned! - Bird sacrifices disprove this, since they are less strict than the animal sacrifices, and they do become invalid with time. - Birds are no proof, because they require a kohen. To dispel all these arguments, the Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/7-11.htm">This is the law of the peace offerings</a>” - to be applied both inside and outside the Temple.<br />
<br />
Art: Frans Snyders - Concert of Birds</span>

---

### content/zevachim/13.txt
<a id="src-00328"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/13.txt`

Zevachim 13 – Errors on Other Steps of the Sacrificial Service
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjecaInbqZI-m8jXNcq7N35ihqmvYQvd-2nVdJ1Z_7t1kSOqhMrkGMMEAxHDqhCQ1-2Vs_-AaCxxix-ot7-a1Zdu0izrhJoF0oSbWoqZCFEVoVbub-nEQp-sLwobtoYnFw2v4kRGfkWmac/s1600/Arthur+Hacker+-+Vale+Or+Farewell.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjecaInbqZI-m8jXNcq7N35ihqmvYQvd-2nVdJ1Z_7t1kSOqhMrkGMMEAxHDqhCQ1-2Vs_-AaCxxix-ot7-a1Zdu0izrhJoF0oSbWoqZCFEVoVbub-nEQp-sLwobtoYnFw2v4kRGfkWmac/s320/Arthur+Hacker+-+Vale+Or+Farewell.jpg" width="254" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">We have learned before that slaughtering a Passover sacrifice or a sin-offering not for their sake makes them invalid. Now we learn that it is true not only for slaughter, but also for the other three steps of the sacrificial service: receiving the blood in the Temple vessel, walking with that blood to the Altar, and throwing it on the Altar. If any of these steps are done with the intention for a different sacrifice type, this makes the sacrifice invalid.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Tarfon was distressed that he had previously heard from his teacher that there is a difference between the laws of receiving blood and throwing it, but he could not remember what the difference was. Rabbi Akiva deduced three points of difference on his own - for example, if one receives the blood outside the Temple, he is not liable, but if he throws the blood on an altar outside the Temple, he is liable to excision.<br />
<br />
At this Rabbi Tarfon remembered that this was what he had learned and exclaimed, “Akiva, whoever parts from you is like one who parts from his life!”<br />
<br />
Art: Arthur Hacker - Vale Or Farewell<br />
</span>

---

### content/zevachim/14.txt
<a id="src-00329"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/14.txt`

Zevachim 14 – Walking with the Blood
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiUNs0E7vIC1emhmSqaHSjJ-DLdeCIw0xeDhx4nkCsUZ2CABbfVP_I6ZsrOzYWS7hnIsrxj58mb1DunL4nLo1gCI6qDYDbthSADAyMiRRd5-kotAxbuCaG4jB-6b33Spsb6IiSog0Vvwsc/s1600/David+Roberts+-+Hall+of+Columns%252C+Karnak%252C+from+Egypt.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiUNs0E7vIC1emhmSqaHSjJ-DLdeCIw0xeDhx4nkCsUZ2CABbfVP_I6ZsrOzYWS7hnIsrxj58mb1DunL4nLo1gCI6qDYDbthSADAyMiRRd5-kotAxbuCaG4jB-6b33Spsb6IiSog0Vvwsc/s320/David+Roberts+-+Hall+of+Columns%252C+Karnak%252C+from+Egypt.jpg" width="217" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">According to Rabbi Shimon, if a kohen has the intent that the sacrifice is of a wrong, different type, and he has this intent while walking with the blood to the Altar, the wrong intent does not invalidate it. This is because walking is not a necessary step, and if the kohen is close enough to the Altar, walking may be altogether absent.<br />
<br />
Said Resh Lakish, “Rabbi Shimon agrees about those offerings that are slaughtered in the Courtyard and then carried inside the Temple Hall (such as Yom Kippur offerings) that the wrong intention does invalidate them – since this walking cannot be circumvented. <br />
<br />
Seeing that walking has somewhat lenient requirements, they asked Rav Chisda if it can be done by a non-kohen. Rav Chisda said that it can, quoting “<a href="http://bible.cc/2_chronicles/35-11.htm">and they slaughtered the Passover offering, and the kohanim threw the blood from their hands</a>” - it must be that the non-kohanim who slaughtered also walked with the blood! However, Rav Sheshet disproved this, and as far as the quote, he explained that the non-kohanim just stood like pillars but did not move at all.<br />
<br />
Art: David Roberts - Hall of Columns, Karnak, from Egypt</span>

---

<a id="src-00330"></a>

Zevachim 15 – Carrying without Walking
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhrUQ28wZ0dvQ0hkGOop__ZxoXoBUvWVH6jyjfg5zO_bLuV0QWycaao3scqCM5gB1nJbSaXWDtol2GGV-FudvinZ75f67yCIhmU7n6uNP4uCiTXD-688y7EUdLt3qvKEy9TFevtljlyPbg/s1600/Jan+Victors+-+Hannah+Giving+Her+Son+Samuel+to+the+Priest.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="291" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhrUQ28wZ0dvQ0hkGOop__ZxoXoBUvWVH6jyjfg5zO_bLuV0QWycaao3scqCM5gB1nJbSaXWDtol2GGV-FudvinZ75f67yCIhmU7n6uNP4uCiTXD-688y7EUdLt3qvKEy9TFevtljlyPbg/s320/Jan+Victors+-+Hannah+Giving+Her+Son+Samuel+to+the+Priest.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a Kohen carries the blood of a sacrifice without walking, that is, he stands in place and hands the blood to another person who is closer to the Altar, is this a valid service? <br />
<br />
They tried to answer this question based on another rule: if a Kohen is sitting, he is disqualified from carrying the blood. It must be, therefore, that when he is standing, he can carry the blood! - No, because maybe by "sitting" the rule means moving by dragging himself in a sitting position. No proof can be deduced from here!<br />
<br />
They tried to answer the question from a different rule: on Passover, the sacrifice would be slaughtered by its owner, and a Kohen would receive the blood, pass it to his fellow, and so on until it reached the Altar. We see from here that one does not have to walk! - No, we don't see it - perhaps they moved a little. Then why were they many? The service of God is better with many.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yochanan concluded, "Conveying the blood without moving one's feet is not a valid service."<br />
<br />
Art: Jan Victors - Hannah Giving Her Son Samuel to the Priest</span>

---

<a id="src-00331"></a>

Zevachim 16 – Who Cannot Do Sacrificial Service
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEin0GYtoxVWENrl4SDzR8hcXVZczxiV8VqZ6o2qsni1BVUmzobfLk_YKEkFnE0AWVriVzE1S2jL6v_kw2o-_Jvn-ba6OrPuPtIFXJ84bxS_WM3Ehyphenhyphen-P1YA4bt1IqnHmz_G6EHOHs3qdzG8/s1600/Pierre+Auguste+Renoir+-+The+Artists+Family.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEin0GYtoxVWENrl4SDzR8hcXVZczxiV8VqZ6o2qsni1BVUmzobfLk_YKEkFnE0AWVriVzE1S2jL6v_kw2o-_Jvn-ba6OrPuPtIFXJ84bxS_WM3Ehyphenhyphen-P1YA4bt1IqnHmz_G6EHOHs3qdzG8/s320/Pierre+Auguste+Renoir+-+The+Artists+Family.jpg" width="256" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The following categories of people, if they receive the blood of the sacrifice, invalidate the offering:<br />
<br />
A non-Kohen. Only the priests who are the descendants of Aharon can serve in the Temple. The Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/22-2.htm">Speak to Aaron and to his sons that they shall separate themselves from the holies of the children of Israel and they shall not profane</a>...” <br />
<br />
A kohen whose relative, one of the seven close ones – father, mother, brother, unmarried sister, son, daughter, or spouse - has died this day. Since Aharon was specifically requested to continue the service after his two sons died, “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/21-12.htm">And he need not leave the Sanctuary and he will not profane</a>...”, we understand that all other Kohanim would profane the service.<br />
<br />
Although the ruling above mentions only receiving the blood, the same disqualification also applies to the other two steps – carrying the blood and throwing it on the Altar. The slaughter, however, is valid if done by a non-Kohen, since the Torah said, “And he slaughters, and a Kohen receives the blood.”<br />
<br />
Art: Pierre Auguste Renoir - The Artists Family<br />
</span>

---

### content/zevachim/17.txt
<a id="src-00332"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/17.txt`

Zevachim 17 – Others Who Cannot Perform Sacrificial Service
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhpcDG95BKqtEMAuTQxxliMVCuy12dJ8HmiwpEVPz9KfVZVJ759mm2tcvgDXbHlskJv4mV8rLma_AqTAVsUdSPsDiVBXMWzj4jD89c9VidEK8G8BX9_-ftVFeIH2pvggpAbIu4IqpiEDuU/s1600/Sir+Edwin+Henry+Landseer+-+Ratcatchers.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="234" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhpcDG95BKqtEMAuTQxxliMVCuy12dJ8HmiwpEVPz9KfVZVJ759mm2tcvgDXbHlskJv4mV8rLma_AqTAVsUdSPsDiVBXMWzj4jD89c9VidEK8G8BX9_-ftVFeIH2pvggpAbIu4IqpiEDuU/s320/Sir+Edwin+Henry+Landseer+-+Ratcatchers.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"><i>One who is ritually impure today</i> (tevul yom), for example,  because of a  contact with a dead rat, has to go to a mikveh. Still, <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/22-7.htm">some vestiges of ritual impurity linger until nightfall</a>. If he receives the blood of a sacrifice, he makes it invalid, because of a verse “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/21-6.htm">They shall be holy... and they shall not profane</a>.”  This verse is extra, and we apply it to the one who is partially impure.</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;"><br />
<i>One who lacks atonement</i>. Some special cases of impurity, such as spiritual leprosy (metzora) require purification in stages, the last stage being bringing the sacrifices. Until he has brought them, he invalidates the service. <br />
<br />
Why did the Torah have to teach both cases, if they are so closely related anyway? - Because each possesses its own stringency, so that the disqualification of one cannot be derived from the other. The “impure today” cannot eat the Kohen's portion, but the one who lacks atonement can. On the other hand, the one who lacks atonement needs a positive action, that is, bringing his sacrifices, whereas the one who is “impure today” only needs nightfall, which comes by itself. <br />
<br />
Art: Sir Edwin Henry Landseer - Ratcatchers</span>

---

### content/zevachim/18.txt
<a id="src-00333"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/18.txt`

Zevachim 18 – A Priest Who is Under-dressed or Overdressed
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiZxP5lCgxUmGvdVUT9lc87R1Pe_m4z7nkonsQgVJLM4TnCr49UhMU3d-KyMNCogsqFS6tGvdOTa_qt_KOx_9DHXV2IkgyIkGEF5wwVnp-4avjAOEHCFvTrIdIaiReKNc6wk0RTLTpT_Us/s1600/John+Bagnold+Burgess+-+The+Favourite+Priest.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="249" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiZxP5lCgxUmGvdVUT9lc87R1Pe_m4z7nkonsQgVJLM4TnCr49UhMU3d-KyMNCogsqFS6tGvdOTa_qt_KOx_9DHXV2IkgyIkGEF5wwVnp-4avjAOEHCFvTrIdIaiReKNc6wk0RTLTpT_Us/s320/John+Bagnold+Burgess+-+The+Favourite+Priest.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Any Kohen priest who lacks the required four priestly garments, invalidates the sacrificial service. The <a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=2">four garments are pants, tunic, belt, and hat</a>. Since the Torah said that “<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/29-7.htm">You shall girdle them with sash and put turbans on them and the priesthood will be for them an eternal law</a>”, we see that when they have all the garments, they are considered priests, but if they lack some, they are considered strangers, and a stranger invalidates the service.<br />
<br />
If they have extra garments, the extra ones invalidate the service because the required garments should be “on the body” and not on other garments. If the garments are too long, too short, or fitting well but shortened by the belt, some say that they are valid, and some say that they are not. However, all agree that if they were too long (dragging) but were shortened by the belt to the desired size, that is fine.<br />
<br />
Art: John Bagnold Burgess - The Favourite Priest</span>

---

### content/zevachim/19.txt
<a id="src-00334"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/19.txt`

Zevachim 19 – Clothes of a Kohen
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjp5fVIbdlcdNbxffp63j3t1E4a4vDfcBS9DltZV4Rt2-hKTYcq25w8KxOwYpXo3sgfX1c0ivxFx5GIJaEKoqJ-LpA2DSwJzdI2qxB5jVRlOeKur86lRg1IW9ntcWGfYau8biqdOtK8o3I/s1600/Peeter+Franchoys+-+Ruby+on+the+Fingernail.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjp5fVIbdlcdNbxffp63j3t1E4a4vDfcBS9DltZV4Rt2-hKTYcq25w8KxOwYpXo3sgfX1c0ivxFx5GIJaEKoqJ-LpA2DSwJzdI2qxB5jVRlOeKur86lRg1IW9ntcWGfYau8biqdOtK8o3I/s320/Peeter+Franchoys+-+Ruby+on+the+Fingernail.jpg" width="254" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A Kohen who has wounded his finger on Shabbat may wrap reed-grass over it if he is in the Temple, where the Sages did not enact additional prohibitions that would complicate the service, but not outside, where one is not allowed to cure non-threatening conditions on Shabbat.<br />
<br />
For a Kohen, a small bandage around a wound is forbidden, because it constitutes an extra garment. Another opinion is that an extra garment is only important in the place of garments, or on the right hand, which is used for service.<br />
<br />
Rava asked a series of questions. If the wind entered the Kohen's garment, does this invalidate the service because the garment is not “on his body,” or is it a normal manner of wearing? Does a louse constitute interposition between the kohen's body and the garment? The dead one certainly does, but what about a live one? Since it comes and goes, it is like a growth on his body, or, since he does not like it, it is an interposition? What about the dust of the earth, a hand in his bosom, or thread hanging from the garment?<br />
<br />
Art: Peeter Franchoys - Ruby on the Fingernail<br />
</span>

---

### content/zevachim/2.txt
<a id="src-00335"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/2.txt`

Zevachim 2 – For the Sake of Mitzvah
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgoG94pd9XLgA5_JSNwxA6mMzpuSHq-zTHEpVxMeku2asDTcLE4iCpILE998-uwqZSEFkHgflk8_DC2rvn9KErVG1QJqOqBGN9ENZpMa-9PIFmAzU6iDgfVpRwUnkFwzhCD-_7Q5s6-GSQ/s1600/Gerard+Ter+Borch+0-+Woman+Reading+a+Letter+.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgoG94pd9XLgA5_JSNwxA6mMzpuSHq-zTHEpVxMeku2asDTcLE4iCpILE998-uwqZSEFkHgflk8_DC2rvn9KErVG1QJqOqBGN9ENZpMa-9PIFmAzU6iDgfVpRwUnkFwzhCD-_7Q5s6-GSQ/s320/Gerard+Ter+Borch+0-+Woman+Reading+a+Letter+.jpg" width="268" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Every sacrifice in the Temple has to be slaughtered for its own sake, for example, a peace offering has to be slaughtered as such, and not as a burnt offering. However, if one slaughtered them for a wrong designation, they are still valid and the ritual can continue – only they are not counted to fulfill the owner's obligation, so that he has to bring another one.<br />
<br />
Exceptions to this rule are a Pesach sacrifice brought on Passover, and a sin-offering. These two, if slaughtered not for their own sake, are completely invalid.<br />
<br />
Ravina said to Rav Pappa, “It's a pity that you were not within Shabbat boundary and could not come to us Friday night, for Rava asked a great question and resolved it.” What was it?<br />
<br />
Rava found this contradiction: the sacrifice is not counted if slaughtered for a “wrong designation,” but if there is no designation, it is valid. A woman's Get, on the other hand, has to be written expressly for her, but if there is no designation, it is invalid. And he answered: a sacrifice, without a designation, is intended for its sake, but a woman, if not otherwise specified, will continue to be married, and does no intend to be divorced.<br />
<br />
Art: Gerard Ter Borch - Woman Reading a Letter </span>

---

### content/zevachim/20.txt
<a id="src-00336"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/20.txt`

Zevachim 20 - Kohanim Washing their Hands and Feet
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi4peMkj_mnoPNd6PB5Qp10VWfRBEtOYBYprieQwCKloAQULwMMFRJdkewKW1rIRnRmFbzjafOgoqtWtSk2buWWSxOtmnDQp37jvs3umwstrNbTcCwC8dxINFbI1xBYiSOG_8R9Ki4dHS8/s1600/Mattia+Preti+-+Pilate+Washing+his+Hands+1663.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi4peMkj_mnoPNd6PB5Qp10VWfRBEtOYBYprieQwCKloAQULwMMFRJdkewKW1rIRnRmFbzjafOgoqtWtSk2buWWSxOtmnDQp37jvs3umwstrNbTcCwC8dxINFbI1xBYiSOG_8R9Ki4dHS8/s320/Mattia+Preti+-+Pilate+Washing+his+Hands+1663.jpg" width="286" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Every Kohen has to sanctify&nbsp;</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">his hands and feet by</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">&nbsp;washing them from a special large Temple vessel in the morning. Otherwise, his service is invalid.<br />
<br />
Rav Assi could not understand the difference between this washing and the ten washings of the High Priest on Yom Kippur, which accompany his five changes of garments - since they do <i>not</i> invalidate the service. Rabbi Yochanan explained to him that the phrase "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/16-4.htm">and then don them</a>" tells us that the garments are essential, but washing is not. Rav Assi's face lit up. But his joy was premature, because Rabbi Yochanan then said, "and by the same token the morning washing should not be significant."<br />
<br />
Even if a Kohen was offering animal limbs on the Altar all night, Rabbi Yehudah the Prince says that he needs to wash them again at dawn, but Rabbi Elazar the son of Rabbi Shimon says that he does not need to repeat the washing even if he serves for ten days in a row.<br />
<br />
If a Kohen steps out of the Temple, does he need to repeat the washing on return, because he took his mind off the service, or does he not, because he can choose to return any time? No decision is reached.<br />
<br />
Art: Mattia Preti - Pilate Washing his Hands 1663<br />
</span>

---

### content/zevachim/21.txt
<a id="src-00337"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/21.txt`

Zevachim 21 – Kohanim Dipping Their Hands and Feet
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEilW9_rIROprYH8JD7yu0GDFdD6PDCM0e9-6kY2yfhTlCvfQekfwaj8RKdSkar2br0EM8JjTA2UUc_nyZSK2Nb7r7saQeMJKr3cNMGOU1aei7ikmzI5A68LA3AR_Y1NvX5UJmxdKzszf4M/s1600/Edgar+Degas+-+Study+of+hands.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="265" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEilW9_rIROprYH8JD7yu0GDFdD6PDCM0e9-6kY2yfhTlCvfQekfwaj8RKdSkar2br0EM8JjTA2UUc_nyZSK2Nb7r7saQeMJKr3cNMGOU1aei7ikmzI5A68LA3AR_Y1NvX5UJmxdKzszf4M/s320/Edgar+Degas+-+Study+of+hands.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The standard procedure for the kohanim to sanctify their hands and feet in the morning is as follows: the kohen is standing in front of the vessel, he places his hands on his feet, and the water is spilled on them from a spout in the vessel.<br />
<br />
Could they to instead dip their hands and feet into the vessel? Can we derive the answer from another rule: if a kohen dipped his hands and feet in a mikvah, he still needs to sanctify them from the vessel. Can we conclude that it is only after a mikvah that he needs another sanctification? - Not necessarily, maybe dipping in the vessel is also ineffective.<br />
<br />
Then why not state this rule about the vessel, and we will deduce the rule about the mikvah? Because you might have thought that, since one can ritually bathe the whole body in the mikvah, how much more so he is allowed to dip just hands and feet! Therefore, the rule tells you otherwise.<br />
<br />
Art: Edgar Degas - Study of hands</span>

---

### content/zevachim/22.txt
<a id="src-00338"></a>

**Source file:** `content/zevachim/22.txt`

Zevachim 22 – The Water Cistern (Kiyor)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgNMCJF5EcbjGK7P-M8Ft9o8pBbTXxPgR9QN0j2aZnCBapKqPB1x46q7Octu9U9ptgOmdRWKe_QdxHAIjAIZbXdaWL6-IyQm6wDZwQBKn6cDK0NcdEPzdx0HmCGGBcLpfvq_AGjFG12Rg8/s1600/Jean-Baptiste-Simeon+Chardin+-+The+Copper+Drinking+Fountain.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgNMCJF5EcbjGK7P-M8Ft9o8pBbTXxPgR9QN0j2aZnCBapKqPB1x46q7Octu9U9ptgOmdRWKe_QdxHAIjAIZbXdaWL6-IyQm6wDZwQBKn6cDK0NcdEPzdx0HmCGGBcLpfvq_AGjFG12Rg8/s320/Jean-Baptiste-Simeon+Chardin+-+The+Copper+Drinking+Fountain.jpg" width="251" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The Kiyor was a large copper vessel, from which the Kohanim would wash their hands and feet. It had twelve spouts to avoid lines. The water in the Kiyor could come from any source, according to one opinion, but according to another, it had to come from a spring.<br />
<br />
If the water in the Kiyor remained there overnight, it become invalid and had to be replaced. Therefore, they used to lower the Kiyor into a mikvah, with the help of a wheel, just before daybreak, and according to other opinions, at more time periods during the night.<br />
<br />
Any Temple vessel could also be used for sanctifying the Kohen's hands and feet, but a regular non-sacrificial vessel could not. Why? Let's try to prove this by comparison with the copper base, in which the Kiyor stood.  Since this base could not be used for washing the Kohen's hands and feet, even though it was a Temple vessel, isn't  it true that a regular vessel surely could not be used? - No! The base is not made for storing water at all! Rather, this is derived from the word that the Torah used - “from it” - and not from other vessels!<br />
<br />
Art: Jean-Baptiste-Simeon Chardin - The Copper Drinking Fountain</span>

---

### content/zevachim/23.txt
<a id="src-00339"></a>

Zevachim 23 - Uncircumcised in Flesh and Uncircumcised in Heart
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEisb-fmFz3n8PoSQL0hdAXUFbEtxff8AmIH6HhQVOw-IenF41VbBtnhyphenhyphenoXIWWe4H4qi8pJfUvCrxF7PnrqFNnKdEbBjRoRVsFfle1ijNrtDOb9XSZZP6V6wOIiPbOr6j8M5FiIXLcZLRtg/s1600/Charles+Emile+Callande+de+Champmartin+-+Study+of+a+Head+of+a+Corpse.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="258" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEisb-fmFz3n8PoSQL0hdAXUFbEtxff8AmIH6HhQVOw-IenF41VbBtnhyphenhyphenoXIWWe4H4qi8pJfUvCrxF7PnrqFNnKdEbBjRoRVsFfle1ijNrtDOb9XSZZP6V6wOIiPbOr6j8M5FiIXLcZLRtg/s320/Charles+Emile+Callande+de+Champmartin+-+Study+of+a+Head+of+a+Corpse.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Any Kohen who is not circumcised, if he serves in the Temple, makes the sacrifices invalid. This is true even if he had a valid reason not to be circumcised, such as if his brothers had died on account of circumcision.<br />
<br />
In addition, any Kohen who is "estranged from his Father in Heaven," that is, who turned away from Torah observance, should not serve in the Temple, and if he does, his sacrifices are invalid. This is learned from the phrase in Ezekiel, "Uncircumcised in flesh and uncircumcised in heart". A questions was asked - and before Ezekiel ben Buzi, did the estranged Kohanim serve in the Temple? Of course not! Then how can we learn a new law from a prophet? We know that Moses taught all the laws the Torah, and they were not changed! - Yes, Moses taught it, but it was an oral tradition, until Ezekiel came and wrote it down.<br />
<br />
Any kohen who is ritually impure invalidates the service. This is true only of impurity caused by a dead dead animal, such as a rat, but the impurity of a human corpse, since it is permitted under some circumstances, does not invalidate the service. Additionally, a Kohen who performs service while sitting invalidates the sacrifices. <br />
<br />
Art: Charles Emile Callande de Champmartin - Study of a Head of a Corpse</span>

---

### content/zevachim/24.txt
